Random Notes

The Riddle of Cooling Off (Part 2)

— Lu

Gentlemen who are cooling off, we meet again in this small garden.

Whether you guessed the three riddles offered last time or not, I cannot help but expose this illusion myself and reveal all the answers:

(1) Under the scorching sun, singing the tune of the lawless emperor, is the cicada. The hotter the sun, the louder the cicada's song, just chirping "I know, I know" without end! Therefore, the cicada's alias is "I know." Some write it as 𧊄蟟. The emperor's tune of the past only made "I know, I know" his mantra. The cicada is also singing "I know, I know," only lacking the word "way," so it is said to be the lawless emperor. This riddle is easy to guess as Puyi, who relies on the power of the scorching sun. In fact, Puyi is also a pathetic creature, no different from the cicada singing "I know, I know." When autumn cools down and the power of the scorching sun wanes, I fear he will also become a silent cicada after autumn.

(2) After Shigemitsu Mamoru's leg amputation, a saying from the Zuo Zhuan lost its effectiveness. This saying is called: "Even the sunflower can protect its foot." Because the sunflower leaves turn towards the sun, preventing sunlight from reaching its roots, there is a saying that the sunflower can protect its foot. Shigemitsu Mamoru lost his foot, so the sunflower cannot protect his foot! Therefore, the saying from the Zuo Zhuan lost its effectiveness.

(3) Aid Ma Yuan, Ma Yuan can be paired with lament. Lament Niu Ai, Niu Ai. The upper couplet, read forwards or backwards, is these five characters: the lower couplet, read forwards or backwards, is also these five characters. In the upper couplet, Ma Yuan is an ancient person, used to compare to the anti-Japanese General Ma Zhanshan; in the lower couplet, Niu Ai is also an ancient person. The Huainanzi says that Niu Ai fell ill for seven days and transformed into a tiger, and so on. Used to compare to Niu Lan, who used hunger strikes to coerce, is clearly an act of a lamentable party, but he can also be called Niu Ai. Because the Niu couple is on a hunger strike, some people lament them and want to find a way to rescue them from danger. Therefore, lament Niu Ai, Niu Ai. The five characters are also related to the current situation. Furthermore, it was recently heard in Shanghai that a yellow ox waiting to be slaughtered escaped halfway and knelt down in a factory, begging the factory owner with tears streaming down its face. The factory owner was moved and bought it, taking it to the release station to save its life. This yellow ox that knelt down to beg can also be called Niu Ai, and the factory owner saving its life is also lament Niu Ai, Niu Ai. The only difference is that the Niu couple on a hunger strike and the Niu who knelt down are one a fake Niu and one a real Niu.

Entrusting to Mrs. Ayscough

— Qu Cheng

Next to the Jade Buddha Temple, in the middle of Binlang Road, there is a black lacquer shikumen. The gatehouse is carved with Li Bai and Du Fu playing chess. This is the residence of the daughter and son-in-law of the late British merchant, "Hui Defeng." The son-in-law's surname is Ayscough, and his name is Florence. Florence Ayscough was formerly a clerk in the Hui Defeng Company. He was aloof in nature and quite capable in handling affairs. Because of this, he gained the favor of the daughter. After their marriage, the daughter's father died of old age, and this enormous inheritance also passed to Ayscough through his wife.

The lady has always enjoyed studying Chinese literature, and even in her diet and daily life, she only finds pleasure in things that are "non-Chinese." Through more than ten years of research, she has gained considerable insights into Chinese poetry and prose. She is engaged in translating Tang poems to introduce them to people in her country. A certain university in Canada heard of her name and awarded her a doctoral degree.

Since then, the lady has been even more diligent in her studies, and her name has become increasingly famous. Whenever she lectures, there are always tens of thousands of listeners. She has broadcasted on radio stations to various countries, and her words all praise Chinese propriety. She especially promotes the old virtues of "chastity" and "three obediences and four virtues" for women. The lady even sets an example for her husband, and she is no less than Meng Zhuang to Liang Hong.

Through the lady's years of loud calls, scholars and women in her country have gradually paid more attention to her scholarship. In this way, there will definitely be many people who will follow in the lady's footsteps and promote her teachings. Now that our modern women are despising the inherent virtues, compared to the lady who cherishes them as treasures, can we not feel ashamed?

Summer Jottings

— Zhi Zheng

In recent days, the temperature in Shanghai has suddenly increased, reaching 103 degrees at its hottest, a new record not seen since the beginning of the year. As a result, the people of Shanghai are seeking ways to escape the heat. Here are some of the most interesting and novel methods, also to add to the conversation while enjoying watermelon and plum juice.

Sudden Rain at Zhaofeng Park The best places to escape the heat in Shanghai are the four major parks, especially Zhaofeng Park, with its dense shade and clear springs, which is most popular among Chinese and Westerners. Therefore, every day at sunset, when the cicadas sing in the evening, Zhaofeng Park becomes a gathering place for men and women, strolling arm in arm, resembling a fairy realm. One day, the heat was sweltering, and the intense heat felt like roasting. At 5:00 PM, the gates of Zhaofeng Park were already crowded with traffic. To entertain visitors, the park hired a Western band to play music, charging a fee of 40 cents. The seats were also filled with listeners. Just as the music began at 5:30 PM, dark clouds suddenly gathered, and heavy rain poured down. As a result, before the end of a song, both the performers and the attendees fled in a panic. The scene of chaos was truly indescribable. I was on my way to the zoo at the time, and I looked around for a place to shelter, so I temporarily stood under a giant tree, hoping to find a moment's peace under the dense shade. However, the rain became heavier and heavier, becoming torrential after a quarter of an hour. My shirt was completely soaked, and my straw hat was filled with water, almost like a drowned chicken. At that moment, the cries of women and the screams of children blended together, echoing the sound of wind and rain. After half an hour, the rain subsided slightly, and I walked out of the park gate. The young women in their thin, cicada-wing-like fashions were especially drenched. Everyone cried out that the heavens were not being kind.

Quick Ferry Across the Huangpu River After visiting the park for a long time, I felt dispirited. A friend proposed a night ferry across the Huangpu River. As soon as the idea was proposed, more than ten people responded, each bringing their families. At 8:30 PM, the group gathered at the Bund bronze statue pier and boarded the Public Utilities Bureau ferry in single file. The ferry was divided into two classes. The highest class was called the special class, mostly occupied by Westerners, with a round trip fare of $1.50. The next class was the first class, with a round trip fare of 80 cents. As the ferry sailed, a refreshing breeze gently brushed against our clothes. Soon, we moved further away from the bustling city area of Shanghai. We only saw three or five fishing boats drifting in the middle of the river, and the opposite bank was shrouded in mist, making it impossible to discern what was there. After a while, the bright moon rose, as large as a wheel, and the rippling river reflected its dazzling light. We leaned against the railing and reminisced about the past, the heat completely gone. Mr. and Mrs. Xiaoguang distributed the food they had prepared to their friends, and we sat together happily, enjoying unlimited joy. The boat traveled for half an hour and docked at Donggou. After 15 minutes, it sailed back up the river and arrived at Gaoqiao around 9:00 PM. We disembarked together. At that time, the river breeze was gentle, as if it were early autumn. We walked for about four minutes and arrived at a hotel. The electric lights were bright, and the furnishings were quite good, with cold snacks and refreshments available inside, but the prices were very high. We went to a teahouse to drink tea and sat around for half an hour. The river moon was like a painting, and the rural scenery under the clear sky was especially beautiful. We returned to the boat at 11:00 PM, all worldly concerns gone. The wind picked up, and amidst laughter and song, we returned to Shanghai after midnight.

Remembering Dinghu Mountain Amidst the Sweltering Heat

— Zizai

Dinghu Mountain in Zhaoqing is a famous mountain in South China, also known as the seventeenth blessed place in the world by Buddhists. Surrounded by mountains, the scenery is magnificent. Ancient trees are lush and dense, blocking out the sunlight. Hidden in the mountainside is a majestic ancient temple covering 30 acres, called Qingyun Temple. The carved beams and painted buildings are incredibly grand. The temple has more than 300 monks, and the number of workers and children is also similar. Inside, there are dozens of elegant guest rooms for tourists to stay. To the left of the temple is a waterfall that thunders through the valley and flows for a thousand feet. On the mountain peak is the always cloud-protected Laodinghu Temple. There are many famous scenic spots and historical sites in the mountains. For example, on the Xixin Pavilion, there is a horizontal plaque with the inscription "Wash Away Impurities" personally inscribed by Zhang Taiyan when he visited during the Bingchen National Protection War. In the guest hall on the side of the Daxiong Hall, there are couplets written by Sun Yat-sen, "Equality of All Beings" and "All Sentient Beings," and a horizontal plaque by Cen Chunxuan, "Deep in the Mountains." Below the steps is a long couplet written by He Ruidan: "As I have heard, the sound of wind, the sound of rain, the sound of springs, the sound of birds, harmonize with the sound of Zen throughout the courtyard. Entering this gate, one suddenly understands." "As can be seen today, the colors of mountains, the colors of clouds, the colors of trees, and the scenery of the four seasons. Arriving at this place, all colors are empty." Completely natural and refined, unusually fitting. There are also the world's unique campanula flowers and five-colored azaleas, Dendrobium loddigesii, and Impatiens urophylla in the mountains, countless rare flowers and exotic herbs, many of which can be used as medicine. Climbing up from Luo Yin's Spring to the mountain takes a journey of 18 li to reach Qingyun Temple. Along the way, birds chirp and springs murmur. The mountains are full of lush greenery, and a gentle breeze comes from time to time, warm in winter and cool in summer, sweeping away all worldly concerns. In the Feishui Pool, a gentle breeze blows, and fine waves float. The water is clear and bottomless. Swimming and bathing is refreshing to the heart and spleen. The sound of bells and the shadows of trees clear all thoughts. One almost feels like they are in the Guanghan Palace and no longer knows the intense heat of summer. Every summer, the number of tourists is no less than that of Mogan Mountain in Zhejiang and Lushan Mountain in Jiangxi, and the famous summer resorts such as Qingdao and Beidaihe in the north. I have visited three times, staying for a month each time. Whenever I remember the past during the summer, I am always fascinated. As I put down my pen here, a cool breeze rustles, as if I am in the Mianlu Pavilion. But thinking of the passing of Xindan and the farewell of Huikong, thinking of the new and feeling the old, feeling the previous battles, even in the sweltering heat, I cannot help but have autumn thoughts.

Worth Introducing National Goods Factories (12)

— He Gongxing

(2) (1) Coal Ball Factory

Coal was invented in our country. Originally, it was a utilization of waste. At first, the sea coal industry king, Mr. Liu Hongsheng, saw that it was a pity to discard coal dust. He spent 5,000 yuan to order Japanese people to build machines for manufacturing coal balls. Once built, he established the China Coal Ball Factory. Business was booming. Up to now, China has factories one, two, and three. It's up to the people. This must be credited to Mr. Liu's vision and perseverance.

There are more than ten coal ball factories in Shanghai, such as China, China, Greater China, Greater China, Far East, Huacheng, Guohua, and Nanyang. Most of them are in Pudong and along Xushe Road.

Coal balls are clean and fire-resistant, and people are happy to use them. However, they must be made of white coal dust. The stoves that burn coal balls mostly have no chimneys, so the dust from bituminous coal cannot be used. When making coal balls, yellow soil must be mixed with the coal dust. Yellow soil from Suzhou is best, because it is sticky and loose. On the one hand, it is easy to solidify, and on the other hand, it is easy to burn. Yellow soil from other places cannot compare. Some say that flammable materials are mixed in the coal balls, but this is nonsense. Two to three percent of yellow soil can be mixed with each ton of coal dust, but it is best to mix 1.7 percent. Too much will not only make it less fire-resistant, but also make it difficult to light. In fact, the quality of coal balls depends not only on the quality of the coal, but also on the amount of yellow soil mixed in.

Our country produces a lot of white coal, but it is still in short supply. If coal dust is used to make balls on a large scale, it will certainly not be enough. In addition to buying a small amount of white coal dust from Shanxi, most of it comes from Annam. Japan has a lot of bituminous coal, which cannot be used.

Our country's machinery factories can now copy coal ball manufacturing machines. The machines come in different sizes. Some produce 114 balls per rotation, some 140, and some 160. The price is around 2,000 yuan.

Although coal balls can be made by hand, like beating charcoal, if you want to sell them, you must use machines. The entire machine is divided into three parts: (1) a grinding machine, (2) a mud mixing machine, and (3) a ball making machine. The coal dust must go through the above three steps to become a ball, and then it falls from the lower part of the ball making machine like rain. It is then dried on a wire mesh screen in a baking oven and manually loaded into baskets.

The above machines produce 30 to 40 tons of coal balls per day. The market price is around 24 yuan per ton. The market price of Annam coal dust is around 11 taels per ton.

Financial and Gold Market Re-emerges with Sharpness

Increased by 6.8 Taels

Exceeding 750 Taels Transacted. Yesterday, the 27th, the gold market demonstrated vibrancy, with transactions proceeding swiftly and methodically. Initially, the market was calm, but later it showed its sharpness, with a difference of up to 6.5 taels between the high and low prices within half a day. The opening prices were slight, but eventually the prices climbed nearly 7 taels. Although the price of large bars rose at the start, it did not cause any disturbance. This was because the silver price did not move, and the futures silver price fell. Subsequently, the price remained between 746 taels and 747 taels, and there were no bulk transactions from various parties. Furthermore, bid tickets went from stable to tight, and there were rumors of a certain bank selling off spot goods. As a result, major players suddenly began to compete to buy, and the buying interest surged, causing the market to become very aggressive and exceed 750 taels. Finally, the price slightly decreased. Later in the day, due to the intense heat and the lack of foreign exchange market activity, the market was temporarily suspended for half a day, and it was expected that normal operations would resume once the weather cooled down. Below is a record of the morning's activities.

High Opening Prices Observed Early On. The market opened with a rise of 2.9 mace for September contracts, reaching 747.5 taels. Although the British bank rate was reported to be 1/8 higher, the American bank's public telegrams were as before, and private telegrams were slightly higher at 1/16. Moreover, the exchange rate suddenly fell by 1.125 points, causing sellers to become excited. Companies such as Yi Feng Yong, Yuan Heng, Yuan Mao Yong, Heng Chang Yong, and Zhi Feng Yong all sold off, causing the price to fall by 1.67 mace. However, there were only a few mace fluctuations, totaling only 45.8 taels. The exchange rate was flat. The initial closing price for U.S. dollars for this month was 81.25, followed by banks buying at 81.25 for August and 30.0125 for October. Both buying and selling were possible. Market participants such as Hong Kang Yong, Yu He, Yuan Xing Yong, Heng Yu, and Yi Feng Yong all bought, while Tong Tai Chang and Heng Chang Yong sold. The market price fluctuated slightly by 7-8 mace, reaching 46.8 taels at 9:15. Later, HSBC offered U.S. dollars for August at 8.75 and for October at 0.0625, and Yokohama Specie Bank and Holland traded English gold for September at 1.825. Therefore, the price returned to 46 taels. At 9:30, HSBC's listed price for English gold remained unchanged, while U.S. dollars decreased by 0.125, resulting in a slight squeeze on the exchange rate. Rui Xing, Yi Feng Yong, Fu Tai Heng, and Yuan Tai all bought, adding one tael. At 10:00, the price was 47 taels, after which the market became mediocre, with fluctuations of no more than 5-6 mace. There were also no large transactions from various firms. Subsequently, due to selling from Tong Tai Chang, Da De Cheng, and retail investors, and because Yokohama Specie Bank sold English gold for October to HSBC at 1.83125, the price retreated by 7-8 mace, reaching 46.2 taels at 10:30. Then the market became peaceful. After 11:00, there were inquiries about wheat firms trading forward for November exchange rates at 3.560, and Yuan Kang Xiang, Tian Feng Yong, Heng Yu, Yuan Xing Yong, Da Xing Yong, Yi Yu, Yu He, Hong Kang Yong, Tong Chun, Yong Feng, Heng Xing, Zhi Feng Yong, Qian Chang Xiang, and others showed strong buying interest. In addition, retail investors who had sold in the morning had to chase after the price, as U.S. dollars became tighter. Banks were buying at 75 for this month.

Bank Buying of Spot Goods Further Boosts Market Sentiment. It was also reported that a certain bank sold off 420 bars of spot goods, greatly improving market sentiment. The price soared, jumping by 6 taels, with only a few mace retracement. At 11:50, the price suddenly reached 52.3 taels. Instantly, Heng Xing, Yi Feng Yong, Yuan Mao Yong, Tong Tai Chang, and others sold off, while buyers retreated. It was also heard that HSBC offered Citibank for October at 30 yuan. Therefore, the price was suppressed to 51 taels after five minutes. At noon closing, the price was 51.4 taels, and then it reached around one tael. Articles were traded at a small amount of 4 mace. Compared to the previous day, the listed price increased by 6.8 taels. The maximum price during the half-day was 52.3 taels (which was unexpected), and the minimum price was 45.8 taels, a difference of 6.5 taels. New York Stock Market Reacts with Slight Decline

(Report by American Eastern Banking Corporation)

On Tuesday, the New York stock market opened higher than the previous day, but the selling trend gradually increased, which was a profit-taking move by short-term traders. Although the decline was not very severe, the volume reached 1.5 million shares. It was also the dividend announcement date for U.S. Steel, and most traders were nervous and suspended activities to wait for the news. Subsequently, the company finally announced that it would only pay dividends on preferred shares and would continue to suspend dividends on common shares. After the news was released, the company's stock immediately fell by one point. However, because the time was late, there were no other effects. But it is believed that most people were not greatly disappointed, because most people had already anticipated it. The decline in the stock market on Tuesday was welcomed in the real economy, as it would allow more people who intended to buy but missed the opportunity at a lower price to join in. Based on the current situation, the profit-taking seems not to be completely stopped, but it is believed that this reaction will soon recover. The Dow Jones index is attached as follows:

Hardware Prices Soar

Hardware prices have been soaring in recent days. According to investigations, the reasons for the price increases are partly due to a shortage of inventory and partly due to wealthy colleagues in the financial industry buying up goods, leading to a perceived shortage of spot goods in the market and skyrocketing asking prices. However, actual sales volumes are quite limited. Thick English galvanized iron, such as #24, can be sold for 10.05 taels per picul, an increase of 1.2 taels compared to before; #26 is 11.25 taels, 0.75 taels higher; #28 is 11.5 taels, also 0.25 taels higher; 3'7" is 0.09 taels, and 3'6" is 0.08 taels, each increasing by 0.02-0.03 taels. Ninety-pound English tinplate can be sold for 10 taels, and 100-pound for 11.5 taels. Ninety-pound American tinplate sells for 13 taels, and 100-pound for 15 taels, each increasing by several cents. Only Huisi iron and the like have not seen major fluctuations. In addition, new lead wire prices are also rising sharply, with #16 to #20 selling for 13 taels, and #21 to #25 selling for 17.75 taels. Prices in other markets have remained relatively stable. Flat galvanized iron sheets with thinner patterns are moving, while those with thicker patterns are not. Market conditions in other areas remain generally lackluster. Due to sluggish sales in other markets, there is no significant difference in market conditions.

Local News

First Meeting of the Research Association for Abolishing the Tael and Changing to the Yuan Held Yesterday

Opinions on the New Currency System Not Yet Unified

A Continued Meeting Scheduled for This Saturday to Discuss

The issue of abolishing the tael and changing to the yuan. Since Minister of Finance Song Ziwen came to Shanghai and exchanged views with various banking and financial circles in the city, three principles have been established. A research committee has been specially formed, consisting of seven Chinese and foreign experts. Banks, financial firms, and the Chamber of Commerce have also been invited to send representatives to participate in discussions and gather opinions for the government's reference. The first research meeting was held at 3 PM yesterday on the third floor of the Central Bank and adjourned at approximately 5 PM. A continued discussion is scheduled for this month on the 30th (Saturday) afternoon at the same location. Details are as follows:

Committee Members Present: Those present at yesterday's meeting included committee members Chen Jian'an, Bei Songsun, Hu Bijiang, Keimo, Mai Zhaote, and Lei Qi, totaling six people. Representatives from the financial industry Yu Zuoting, the Chamber of Commerce Ma Jiliang, committee member Liu Hongsheng, and the Bank Association Hu Mengjia were all absent due to other commitments.

Meeting Proceedings: The meeting commenced at 3 PM, chaired by Chen Jian'an. The chairman began with a report, stating that the committee is of a research nature. Regarding the issue of abolishing the tael and changing to the yuan, the three principles established by Minister of Finance Song after referring to opinions from various circles will be further studied in depth to provide recommendations for the government's adoption. Following the report, committee members and representatives expressed their opinions. Regarding the issuance of the new currency, their attention was focused on the Currency Regulations. Because the government promulgated Currency Regulations in the third year of the Republic (1914), which stipulated a weight of more than 7.2 mace, the subsequent minting of new coins did not fully comply with the regulations, leading to confusion in the market currency. Although the recent sharp decline in foreign coins was due to the decline in domestic production and the concentration of spot goods in Shanghai, the confusion of hard currency and the inconsistency of weight were important reasons. Therefore, the minting of new coins after the abolition of the tael and the change to the yuan must not only seek uniformity in fineness but also comply with the regulations of the third year of the Republic to prevent the people from suffering invisible losses. Furthermore, attention must be paid to the minting of subsidiary coins to implement the decimal system and facilitate transactions for the people. On the other hand, some opinions considered that the minting costs required for recoining new coins would be enormous, which the government would find difficult to bear amidst the current internal and external troubles. Therefore, they believed that it was necessary to reduce the weight of the new coins to compensate. If this were the case, the burden on the people would increase, and it would seem contrary to the government's intention to benefit the people by abolishing the tael and changing to the yuan. Therefore, individual opinions were not yet unified. It was decided to continue the discussion at the original location at 2:30 PM on the 30th of this month.

Chen Xingzhi's Remarks: According to committee member Chen Xingzhi, who spoke to a reporter from the Central News Agency, today's meeting was entirely of a research nature, so there were no resolutions. All three principles have been carefully studied. Regarding the manufacturing of legal tender, there are proponents of the system of the third year of the Republic and proponents of other systems. Opinions from all sides differ, so detailed research is necessary because the issue is very important.

Liu Hongsheng's Letter: The original letter from Liu Hongsheng is translated as follows: "To Mr. Chen Jian'an of the Central Bank, I regret to inform you that I am ill today and unable to attend the meeting of the Abolishing the Tael Committee this afternoon. I would like to briefly state my views on the minting fee. In my opinion, in order to maintain the operation of the mint and cover expenses given today's high prices, the minting fee should not be lower than 2%. The reasons are as follows: (1) The mint should not incur losses due to minting. A minting fee of 2% seems sufficient to cover labor and unforeseen expenses. (2) The mint cannot be sure that it will have work throughout the year. Ample preparation should be made to maintain the operation of the factory. (3) Based on my experience, the actual costs of the factory often exceed its estimated costs. Therefore, with regard to minting, the minting fee should be estimated generously. (4) The mint estimates that it can mint 13 million yuan of silver dollars per month, but according to my estimation, it will be no more than 10 million yuan. In this case, setting the minting fee at 2% is even more necessary. With sincere regards, Liu Hongsheng."

Gerhard's Opinion: The letter from expert Gerhard (i.e., Keimo) to Chen Jian'an regarding the abolition of the tael is translated as follows: "Regarding the three points raised by Minister Song, I was instructed by the committee members at the meeting on July 20 of the 21st year to summarize various relevant points. I have followed the instructions and recorded the key points of the opinions and proposals made by the committee members as follows: (1) Regarding the weight and fineness of the new currency, it has become a unanimous consensus that the new currency should be the sole and universal monetary unit in China's loan system before China changes from the silver standard. In this case, the mixed-color silver coins currently circulating throughout the country should be gradually recalled and recoined. Assuming that the total amount of silver coins in the country is 200 million yuan, the cost of collecting, melting, and recoining these 200 million yuan will be at least 1.25%. The national treasury will inevitably incur an additional expenditure of 25 million yuan. However, the above estimate does not include the transportation costs from remote areas to the Shanghai Mint, nor does it consider the statutory tolerance of 0.5%, which includes both weight and fineness. Although it is undesirable to have it necessarily at the time of the initial issuance of new coins, it cannot be guaranteed that it will not exist in the silver coins currently in circulation. With the above-mentioned circumstances, the lowest cost of implementing the new policy must be compensated. Even if the government authorities do not pay for this, the situation is inevitable. This minimum cost should be around 1.75%. Based on the above reasons, it is proposed to change the weight and fineness of the current circulating currency as follows: current weight 415 grains, current fineness 0.890, proposed new weight 412 grains, proposed new fineness 0.880. Calculated according to the composition of the new proposal, the total weight is 3 grains lower, i.e., 0.723%, and the fineness is 10 lower, i.e., 1.846%, which can compensate for the recoining cost and take into account the aforementioned statutory tolerance. The weight of the new currency should be calculated in grams. If the weight of the new national currency is 412 grains, then it should be expressed as 26.6971 grams in grams. If the fineness is 0.880, then the pure silver it contains should be 23.493448 grams. Assuming that the composition of the new currency is as above, then its true value should contain 0.6992305 Shanghai taels, but the minting cost has not been calculated. The minting cost should be determined by the mint authorities, but it should also depend on the size of the coinage. (2) The exchange rate for silver contracts still in effect. In order to be fair, this exchange rate should be based on the true value of the new national currency. According to the true value of 100 new national coins... Shanghai taels, 69.92305, plus the minting cost, assuming it is 1.5%, Shanghai taels, 1.04884, totaling 70.97189 Shanghai taels. The above calculations are hypothetical for both parties to the silver contract. Ultimately, what rate should the silver contract be based on in order to convert silver into silver coins? The opinions of bankers, industrialists, and merchants should be widely solicited before a decision is made. The resolution of this issue is unlikely to cause any difficulties. (3) What measures should be taken to make society understand and trust this reform? The most important ones are roughly the following: (A) The new national currency should have freedom of transportation between the provinces of China or between China and foreign countries. Since this new currency represents the monetary unit of the Chinese silver standard, before China's currency system changes from the silver standard, neither the new currency nor raw silver with a fineness of less than 0.880 should be prohibited from entering or exiting freely. (B) Freedom of minting. Freedom of minting has one meaning: the Shanghai Mint can exchange the currently circulating currency for new coins at any time, as long as the old coins still retain their original statutory weight and have not been stripped or otherwise damaged. Freedom of minting also has one meaning: the mint can exchange sycee for new coins at any time according to the initially announced conversion rate (a time limit may be added to this exchange to promote the elimination of sycee). Freedom of minting also has one meaning: if someone requests to exchange large bars of silver with a fineness of less than 0.997 for new national coins, the mint can purchase the national coins it should pay at any time and can easily determine it once using the following formula: national currency 1.000 ounce 0.999 fineness, 1 ounce, 480 grains (412 grains 0.880 fineness), 1 national currency, the answer equals foreign currency 1.322.5948. This is a fixed number that will never change. The minting fee should be deducted from this fixed number. (C) Minting silver bars. If the Shanghai Mint can mint silver bars, it will be of great benefit. This silver bar should still have its original fineness of 0.999. Its value, including the copper cost of minting 1000 yuan of silver coins, should be equal to 1000 yuan of national currency. The silver bar should have the mint's seal, number, and the fineness and weight should be marked prominently. This silver bar has two functions: first, for clearing purposes, to avoid counting and identifying silver coins and to facilitate transactions; second, for export purposes when possible. When China still uses the silver standard, the freedom of silver to enter and exit is necessary. This is very similar to the situation in various gold standard countries where gold bars are more important than gold coins. Gold bars have the freedom to be transported in and out. I personally think this point is very important because in this way, various exchange banks can develop their legitimate business. This is also not harmful to the Chinese government but beneficial because the cost of minting a silver bar worth 1000 yuan is much less than the cost of minting one-yuan silver coins worth 1000 yuan. Anyone who holds or buys a silver bar worth 1000 yuan pays the same coinage tax as anyone else, i.e., the minting fee for minting 1000 yuan of silver coins. Compared with the current situation, this method is not painful for exporters. Anyone who wants to transport silver sycee abroad must also pay a coinage tax, the amount of which may not be smaller than the fee charged by the mint because when silver bars become silver sycee, local silver smelters will inevitably charge a fee. (D) Dismantle other mints in China. Since the Shanghai Mint is sufficient to realize the entire reform plan, there will be no need for other mints in China to exist. Their continued existence will be extremely harmful to the progress of currency unification. If countless other mints cannot be stopped from working, the initial stage of the reform plan will inevitably be affected. Merely closing these mints is not enough to guarantee that they will not compete with the Shanghai Mint in the future. Only complete dismantling can guarantee that they will not destroy the true goal of the new plan. (E) Invite representative groups to actively cooperate. It is proposed to invite leaders from the financial, industrial, and commercial sectors to organize a permanent committee to assist the board of directors of the mint. The board of directors can understand everything about the mint authorities' measures and responses. If the board of directors can appoint a well-known mint chemist who is fair enough to guarantee the composition of the new currency, it will greatly benefit the progress of the business and easily create general trust. (F) The sycee reserves should be eliminated immediately. Since the entire plan is closely related to the abolition of the tael, the mint should immediately start recoining the sycee reserves into new coins, then further recoin the large amounts of mixed-color old silver coins, and finally, if necessary, use imported large bars to mint new coins. The above are the points that should be noted. In addition, there may be other points that can be studied, which should be discussed by other relevant parties. Before ending this article, I would like to state that according to my estimate, the total number of silver coins circulating in China is 200 million yuan, while the sycee reserves stored in banks are difficult to exceed 110 million taels. Therefore, even considering the existing silver coins and sycee, the ratio is 92 to 8."

Letter from the Central Mint: The original letter from Wei Jingzhou and Xiao Weide of the Central Mint is translated as follows: "To the Abolishing the Tael Committee, we are writing to inform you that the silver dollar minting fee we have revised is based on minting 10 million yuan per month, with 10 hours of minting per day. The minimum fee must be 2.25% (&225,000). Please refer to the attached estimate. This minting fee should be increased or decreased, and the increase or decrease should be announced. We believe that the Central Mint should retain the right to increase or decrease the minting fee, and the increase or decrease will depend on the amount of coinage and future changes in the weight, fineness, and material prices of silver coins. We wish to state that our estimates do not include any profit. Furthermore, since minting has not yet begun, there is no basis for the current estimate. In order to be cautious, we have specifically revised the calculation of silver loss, combining it with the copper loss. We believe that the silver loss must be based on 2.5 ounces lost per 1000 ounces of silver per month for 12.5 million ounces of silver per month, because minting 10 million yuan of silver coins requires melting 12.5 million ounces of silver, and there will inevitably be 40% to 50% of waste falling off during the molding process, of which only 50% to 60% can be used for minting. This 40% to 50% of waste is still returned to the 'melting department' for remelting into new silver ingots. The copper required for manufacturing silver coins is now revised to 5 jiao per pound. Most of this copper is purchased from overseas, and copper prices and exchange rates fluctuate from time to time, so it must be taken into account in advance. Depreciation and interest on various machines are also included in our calculations, because the equipment for minting machines, engines, etc. was purchased more than ten years ago, and after several years of work, it needs to be replaced, so this depreciation reserve is for the future replacement of new machines. Workers must be trained initially, so the amount of 10 million yuan minted per month cannot be reached immediately. If the amount of coinage is only 50% of the coinage capacity, the monthly income will only be 112,500 yuan. After the mint has reached the point where it can mint fully, whether its monthly income can offset expenses depends entirely on whether the supply of silver for minting silver coins can be continuous. If the supply to the factory is interrupted or insufficient, and therefore it cannot mint as much as possible, the income will also decrease proportionally, and the mint will inevitably suffer losses. Therefore, it is necessary to pay attention to the sufficient and continuous supply of silver, and it is also necessary to plan in advance how to maintain it during periods of suspension and reduction of work. Otherwise, the mint will only have to increase the minting fee according to the minimum amount of coinage. The minting fee we have calculated is not fixed. We hereby declare that this calculation depends entirely on the amount of coinage and the prices of labor and materials. The 2.25% we have estimated is based on the highest amount of coinage. If the silver supplied to the mint by bankers in the future is only 50% of its coinage capacity, the minting fee will naturally have to be increased proportionally. Our goal is to make the mint a self-sufficient factory, like other factories. The most important goal is to mint a national currency with uniform fineness and weight and to train personnel to become an efficient organization. Our goal is to create a skilled organization so that irregular situations do not occur and so that the fineness and weight of the new silver dollar are uniformly reliable. However, we sincerely hope that you will study our estimates in detail and plan for a substantial fund to maintain the operation of the factory, because there must be no mistakes at the beginning of operations. The future of the mint depends entirely on the cooperation of bankers, industrialists, and commercial leaders. Wei Jingzhou and Xiao Weide." Attached: Revised estimate of monthly coinage expenses for the Shanghai Central Mint. Monthly minting of silver dollars: 10,000,000 yuan. Based on minting 4,000,000 yuan per day, 10 hours of minting per day, 25 working days per month. 127. Estimate based on: silver dollar, weight 412 grains, silver 88%, copper 12%. Salaries and wages: 41,300 yuan. Silver verification department expenses: 2,800 yuan. Melting department expenses: 6,900 yuan. Minting department expenses: 9,750 yuan. Steam engine department expenses (including coal): 18,650 yuan. General affairs department expenses: 2,000 yuan. Transportation and testing fees: 800 yuan. Insurance: 1180 yuan. Silver loss: assuming 12,500,000 ounces, 2.5 ounces per 1000 ounces, 31,7250 ounces lost, 1.30 yuan per ounce including copper loss, 75,000 pounds, 0.5 yuan per pound, 40,625 yuan. Copper alloy: 37,500 yuan. Depreciation: 25,540 yuan. Interest: 5,000,000 yuan, annual interest rate of 6%, totaling 300,000 yuan, 25,000 yuan per month. Mold making fee: 1,500 yuan. Total: 213,545 yuan.

Directorate General of Posts Revises Regulations for Mailing Items

Datong News Agency: After the postal blockade in the Northeast, Huang Naishu, Director General of Posts, has revised the regulations for mailing items. The regulations are as follows: (1) Mail to Russia and Asia will be rerouted via Vladivostok by sea. (2) Mail to Korea (leased territory) will be rerouted via Dalian, Japan. (3) Mail to Europe will be rerouted via the Suez Canal as before. Mail from the three eastern provinces with stamps from the three eastern provinces will be treated as underpaid. Mail with Chinese stamps will not be treated as underpaid. The Directorate General has instructed the Shanghai Administration to comply with the above regulations.

Illegal Establishment of Post Boxes by Japanese Residents

First Batch Shipped Out This Morning

Since our country blockaded postal services in the Northeast, Japanese residents in Shanghai immediately established temporary mailboxes to collect and send mail to the Northeast and other locations. Yesterday, they began collecting and delivering letters at the Huangpu Wharf and the Japanese Club. This morning at 9:00 AM, mail processed by the Japanese in Shanghai was shipped out on the Dalian Maru.

Mail Collection Procedures: The temporary post office, jointly established by the Japanese Chamber of Commerce and Industry, the Situation Committee, and various federations in Shanghai, has set up a collection point at the Japanese Club in Hongkou. Mailboxes have also been placed at the Huangpu Wharf, and a Japanese person named Suetaro Okajima has been specially assigned to manage this. It is stipulated that registered items, parcels, and express mail will not be accepted for the time being, only ordinary letters. Chinese postage stamps should be affixed. The first collection deadline was 9:00 AM this morning. Afterwards, mail will be collected for one hour starting at 8:00 AM on the days when the Dalian Kisen Kaisha ships depart. If the deadline is missed, it will be delayed by three days until the next ship departs.

No Postage Stamps Affixed: Yesterday, many letters from Japanese merchants and residents in Shanghai destined for the Eastern Provinces were delivered to the Japanese Club and the Huangpu Wharf. However, none of the letters being sent had postage stamps affixed. When reporters inquired with the Japanese about why they were not affixing postage stamps, the Japanese person stated that although the collection point stipulated that Chinese postage stamps could be affixed, since the delivery was being arranged independently by fellow countrymen, there was no need to pay postage to the Chinese post office again. Rather than spending money to buy Chinese postage stamps, they would rather pay the postage due in the Northeast. Therefore, almost all of the letters being sent this time did not have postage stamps affixed.

Foreign Merchants Refuse to Send: On the 25th and 26th, various foreign firms in this port sent letters destined for the Northeast, Harbin, and Siberia to the Dalian Kisen Kaisha. The president of Dalian Kisen, Shinji Sato, stated that they needed to be redirected to the mailbox at the wharf. The foreign firms took back the original letters, but then worried that entrusting the mail to the Japanese for delivery might lead to disputes, which would be inappropriate. Yesterday, the foreign merchants agreed to continue sending letters to Siberia through the Chinese post office, which would then forward them via Canada. Although this would be slightly delayed by a few days, it would effectively avoid obstructions and complications along the way. As a result, foreign mail has been refused for delivery by the Japanese.

First Batch Shipped Out: The first batch of letters collected by the Japanese temporary post office was due this morning at 9:00 AM. At 9:05 AM, they were packaged and sent aboard the Dalian Maru, to be transported to Dalian Bay. From there, they will be distributed by the South Manchuria Railway to the puppet bureau in Shenyang, and then forwarded to various ports. From 8:00 AM to 9:00 AM this morning, letters destined for the Northeast, Harbin, etc., can still be collected and sent.

Incoming Mail to Shanghai: Regarding the first batch of mail sent from the Northeast to Shanghai and other locations after the puppet state forcibly took over the post office, a telegram was received yesterday stating that it had been loaded onto the Dalian Kisen steamer Fengtian Maru and is expected to arrive at the Huangpu Wharf at 4:30 PM this afternoon. Yesterday, the Japanese residents had already agreed that mail sent from the puppet state would also be collected by the Japanese Club. Letters, parcels, etc., destined for Shanghai would be delivered by coolies hired by the club using bicycles. However, a proper method for forwarding items to various locations in the interior has not yet been agreed upon.

Remittance Procedures: For remittances from Shanghai to various locations in the Northeast, the Japanese residents have reached an agreement with the Hankou Bank to handle the exchanges. Since the Hankou Bank has a temporary contract with the puppet state's post office for postal remittances, the bank can handle exchanges to various locations in the Northeast.

Huang Naishu's Comments: Huang Naishu, the Director of the Postal Bureau, spoke to a reporter from the Xin Sheng News Agency regarding the Japanese establishing a post office. According to his information, the Japanese side does not yet have a clear organization and is simply delivering items via the Dalian Maru. Therefore, this is a matter for the Japanese and does not affect any other party. Furthermore, since Chinese postage stamps are being used, there is no basis for immediate action. If the Japanese side takes xenophobic actions, such as not using Chinese postage stamps or formally establishing a post office, then we will naturally respond according to the law. He is determined not to allow any party to undermine China's postal independence.

Yu and Feixin Confer Again Yesterday on the Case of Roads Built Beyond the Boundary

Our Side Insists on Not Impairing Sovereignty

The Municipal Council Has Reported to the Consular Body

Central News Agency reports that the draft agreement on the recovery of roads built beyond the boundary was previously discussed and agreed upon by Yu Hongjun, Secretary-General of the Municipal Government, and Feixin Dun, Director-General of the Municipal Council. Feixin Dun then submitted it to a special meeting of the Municipal Council Board of Directors on July 6 for discussion. As a result, several points in the draft were revised, and it was then handed back to Feixin Dun and Secretary-General Yu for further discussion. Secretary-General Yu believed that the revisions contradicted our principle that "the sovereignty over roads built beyond the boundary belongs to the Municipal Government." Therefore, on the 18th, he visited Feixin and refuted the revisions made by the Municipal Council Board of Directors. Feixin agreed to submit them to the next Board of Directors meeting for further discussion. At 10:30 AM yesterday, Feixin visited Secretary-General Yu at the Municipal Government again. He proposed to revise the points corrected by Yu on the 18th in preparation for submitting them to the regular meeting of the Municipal Council Board of Directors in the afternoon for discussion. Secretary-General Yu stated his reasons for not being able to revise them and reiterated the principle that "the sovereignty over roads built beyond the boundary belongs to the Municipal Government." After an hour of discussion, Feixin left. Furthermore, the Municipal Council's Information Office announced that at yesterday afternoon's meeting of the Municipal Council Board of Directors, Director-General Feixin Dun reported on the situation of negotiations with representatives of the Municipal Government regarding the agreement on the management of roads outside the boundary. It was then resolved that a copy of the proposed measures would be transcribed and sent to the Consular Body with a letter.

Director-General of the Naval Department, Li Shijia, Departed for Japan Yesterday Morning

The Ninghai Warship's Outstanding Fees Are to Be Paid in Installments

The construction of the Ninghai warship, which the Navy Department commissioned in Japan, has been completed, but a portion of the shipbuilding costs remains unpaid. Therefore, the warship has not been able to return to the country for the time being. Li Shijia, Director-General of the Naval Department, who supervised the construction of the warship, returned to Beijing from Japan in the middle of this month to discuss the matter with Minister Chen Shaokuan. A solution has now been found. Li boarded the Nagasaki Maru yesterday morning for his first trip to Japan. Yesterday morning, a reporter from the Xin Sheng News Agency met with Li Shijia and asked him about the results of his discussions with the Navy Department after returning to Beijing. According to him, at a time when the country's finances are extremely strained, the issue of raising funds was quite hesitant for a time, but ignoring it would greatly affect our credibility. However, the amount owed for the warship, apart from what has already been paid, is not very large. It has now been agreed with Minister Chen to temporarily carry two-thirds of the outstanding warship fees to pay in advance. The remaining amount will be communicated to the factory in a letter from the Ministry, requesting that it be remitted within the month after the Ninghai warship sails back to the country. It is expected that this will not be difficult to arrange, and the warship should be able to sail back to the country by the middle of next month.

Meeting of the Northwest Problem Research Association

First Meeting of the Executive Committee

The Northwest Problem Research Association held its first meeting of the executive committee at the association's office at 3:00 PM yesterday. Those present included Hu Shuhua, Pan Yangyao, Li Dachao, Guo Weiping, Dai Yuzheng, Chen Weixin, and Yin Zhufu. The meeting was chaired by Li Dachao, and the following resolutions were made: (1) To elect Hu Shuhua, Guo Weiping, and Li Dachao as standing committee members; (2) To assign duties to each department, with each department forming a committee in addition to appointing a director; (3) To pass a declaration; (4) To invite Yang Hucheng, Shao Lizi, Deng Binshan, Lu Dachang, Jin Shuren, Lu Xiaozu, Ma Lin, Li Dan, Ma Hongkui, and Sun Weiru (all from the Northwest), and Yu Youren, Shao Yuanchong, Ma Fuxiang, Cai Yuanpei, Li Shizeng, Zhu Qinglan, Wu Tiecheng, Ma Xiangbo, Huang Renzhi, Shi Liangcai, Zhang Gongquan, Qian Xinzhi, Chen Xing, Chen Guangfu, Li Fuxun, Wang Zhixin, and Wu Yunqi (all from the central government and Shanghai) and dozens of others as supporting members of the association; (5) The standing committee members are responsible for handling the various motions passed by the general assembly. The declaration of the inaugural meeting and the bylaws of the association are recorded below:

Declaration of the Inaugural Meeting of the Northwest Problem Research Association: The Northeast has fallen, Rehe is under alarm, and the tyrannical sun rages. The people of the country are united in anger. The Northwest Problem Research Association, which has been in preparation for several months, has also been formally established at this heated and tense time, which is truly a cause for joy and celebration. At the beginning of its establishment, we cannot help but briefly mention a few points to inform the people of the country: (1) Awaken the people of the country's sight and hearing. The Northeast, which is of great importance, fell to the invasion of the tyrannical sun on September 18 because the people of the country did not pay attention to it. Today, the Northwest problem is even more important than the Northeast, but the people of the country still do not pay much attention to it. The problem of overpopulation in the Southeast has led to the inability to solve the unemployment problem. The only way to solve this is to reopen new paths and develop the Northwest to avoid the covetousness of foreigners. It is too late for the Northeast, but the Northwest can still be saved. This is a matter of life and death for the people of the country, and it is what our association's colleagues should urgently awaken the people of the country to. (2) Conduct on-site investigations. As the ancients said, "Sitting and talking is not as good as getting up and doing," and "Hearing a hundred times is not as good as seeing once." Since our colleagues have taken on the task of studying the Northwest problem, they should collect as much information as possible for the use of our colleagues' explorations before conducting research. Our association has dispatched chief members Hu Shuhua and Guo Weiping to go to the Northwest to conduct on-site investigations. They plan to investigate Shaanxi, Gansu, Qinghai, and even the key passes outside the customs separately and provide the information obtained to our association's colleagues for research at any time. (3) Pay attention to scientific research. The biggest illness in our country is the lack of scientific thinking among the people of the country, which has led to all kinds of undertakings being inferior to others. Backward production and declining industries are a cause for regret if we do not change now. After the establishment of our association, we are willing to devote our full efforts to paying attention to scientific research, cultivating the scientific literacy of the people of the country, developing industries, and promoting production so that the underdeveloped industry of China can emulate Europe and the United States and progress steadily every day. (4) Concentrate talents from home and abroad. Our country today appears on the surface to be overstaffed, but in reality, it is difficult to find talent. Mechanical, electrical, mining, metallurgical, civil engineering, forestry, agricultural reclamation, and other specialists are needed everywhere in the country, especially in border areas. Our association hopes to concentrate these talents to engage in the development of the Northwest, and the unemployed compatriots in the prosperous cities can also have a place to work. In this way, countless unemployed compatriots can all have a way out, which is beneficial to people, to the public, and to the private sector. (5) Assist government plans. Our association's investigation findings and research accumulations will not be kept secret or selfishly. We are extremely willing to contribute them to the government as much as possible, hoping that the government will carry out large-scale construction. Our association's colleagues will forget their limitations and do their best to assist the government in preparing various plans to promote their implementation and achieve immediate results. (6) Introduce overseas compatriots to invest. In recent years, the establishment of domestic enterprises has been most difficult due to the fundraising of capital, and overseas compatriots who want to invest in the country have no suitable industry to operate in. The Northwest region has vast land, rich products, and great potential for various undertakings. Overseas compatriots who care about their motherland will surely be happy to invest to promote the progress of the Northwest's production industry. Our association is willing to take on the responsibility of attracting and introducing them. Our association is willing to carry out the six points mentioned above step by step, providing research for the people of the country on the one hand and providing consultation for the government on the other. We attach equal importance to theory and practice, and combine scholarship with action. Given time, we hope to achieve practical results. Fearing that the road will be difficult and that our strength will be weak, we sincerely hope that comrades at home and abroad who are enthusiastic about the Northwest problem will give us their support and work together to make progress. We look forward to it with the utmost sincerity. We hereby declare this.

British and American Consuls Visited Mayor Wu Yesterday

Regarding the Addition of Chinese Members to the Land Commission

According to Article 6 of the Yangjingbang Regulations, the Municipal Council's Land Commission is composed of only three Westerners. Recently, due to the increasing number of affairs, a resolution was made at the last meeting of the two taxpayers' meetings to add two Chinese members, which clearly requires amendment to Article 6. At the same time, according to Article 28 of the same Regulations, changes to the Regulations must be approved by the local government. Therefore, at 9:00 AM yesterday, British Consul-General Beilinan and American Consul-General Keyinhhan went to the Municipal Government to seek approval. They were received by Mayor Wu Tiecheng and Secretary-General Yu Hongjun. After the two consuls explained their intentions, Mayor Wu replied that the Municipal Government not only expressed its approval but also considered it extremely necessary. The addition of Chinese members would inevitably lead to a greater fusion of feelings between Chinese and foreign citizens, and cooperation between Chinese and foreigners would inevitably see greater progress. However, the method of selection, whether it will continue to be selected by the taxpayers' meeting in the future, has not yet been determined and requires a detailed discussion before a decision can be made. The two men left at about 10:00 AM.

Committee Formed to Study Accounting Systems for Various Industries

The Municipal Chamber of Commerce held its third executive committee meeting at 4:00 PM yesterday. Regarding rent reductions voluntarily offered by landlords that exceed the amount permitted by the Municipal Government, in accordance with the principle of contractual freedom, they were not originally restricted by the Municipal Government's announcement. City Council Representatives Petition in Beijing

Regarding the Request to Correct the Municipal Government's Rent Exemption Standards

The Shanghai City Residents' Association, based on the resolution of the 16th Executive Committee meeting regarding rent reduction and exemption, appointed representatives including Zhang Yichen to petition the capital. Representative Zhang departed for Beijing by night train last night. Here is the submitted petition to the Central Party Headquarters, the National Government, and the Executive Yuan:

Petition stating that the rent regulations in Shanghai cannot meet the needs of citizens with weak economic capabilities, requesting review and correction. The Shanghai market has been affected by the global economic downturn, the high value of gold and low value of silver, and floods in various provinces, leading to a situation where citizens appear strong but are actually weak. Furthermore, due to the concentration of cash and the decline of Shanghai industries, real estate has become a source of speculation and a shortcut to wealth. As a result of the high land prices and property values, and the small profit margins, rents have been increased repeatedly, followed by forced evictions. The difficulty for Shanghai citizens to reside and operate businesses has become a major and dangerous problem. The exorbitant costs of small rent, key money, and opening fees are difficult to calculate. Last year, during the floods and the Manchurian Incident, small and medium-sized citizens, despite their weak economic capabilities, showed great patriotism and provided substantial disaster relief and support. However, landlords mostly sat back and enjoyed the benefits without contributing a single penny. Historically, the government has issued public bonds and treasury bills, and all industries have been allocated and required to purchase them, but landlords have always managed to avoid them. Since the January 28th Incident, small and medium-sized citizens have participated in strikes, resisted aggression, and worked tirelessly to provide material and economic assistance to wounded soldiers and refugees. However, landlords fled to Hong Kong or their hometowns, locking their doors and making it impossible to obtain even a single cent of assistance from them. Whether or not they are patriotic is their own business, and it is difficult to force them. However, citizens with weak economic capabilities, whose post-disaster commercial income is less than half of what it used to be, have resorted to reducing food intake, clothing, and salaries. The ever-increasing rents, which account for the largest portion of their expenses, must be reduced and exempted in accordance with the actual needs of citizens with weak economic capabilities. Otherwise, their survival is in jeopardy. During times of commercial prosperity, rents increased steadily, and people had to endure it because it was not easy to close down or move. However, during times of commercial decline, landlords should have automatically reduced rents. However, negotiating with them is like seeking skins from a tiger. To rescue the citizens, the municipal government must correct this. Food is a matter of vital importance, and the government has suppressed high rice prices and punished hoarding and speculation. However, rice can be substituted by other things, and clothing varies in price and can be chosen freely. However, housing has become a semi-monopoly, similar to food and clothing, which is inappropriate. If rents do not correspond to the market, then the hard work of small and medium-sized citizens will only benefit the landlords, and the consequences will be dire. Therefore, rent reduction and exemption in Shanghai is necessary to restore vitality. For this reason, representative Zhang Yichen is dispatched, along with the Municipal Government's rent exemption announcement and the rent reduction measures of the Rent Reduction Movement Committee, to respectfully request review and instructions. We earnestly request that you consider the needs of citizens with weak economic capabilities, correct the Shanghai Municipal Government's rent exemption measures, and secure the prosperity of Shanghai and the survival of its citizens. Respectfully presented to President of the Executive Yuan, Wang...

The Commercial Press Resumes Operations and Employs Personnel

Primarily Employing Former Employees

The Commercial Press Main Factory, Translation Department, and Oriental Library were previously destroyed by Japanese troops. The shareholder meeting resolved that operations would resume on August 1st. This newspaper has reported this previously. It is now reported that the press is preparing to resume operations, and the issue of personnel employment is of great importance. A special personnel committee has been established to oversee everything to ensure careful consideration. Although the press is permitted to employ 20% new employees according to the group agreement law, the press authorities have decided to primarily employ former employees to take care of former colleagues. Therefore, of the approximately 200 employees hired by the press's general management office and distribution department, almost all of them are former colleagues. After operations resume, if business improves, the old employees will be given priority when additional personnel are needed in these two departments. It is also reported that the press is preparing to restore a considerable printing factory, which will soon be ready. The employment of workers will also primarily focus on former employees.

Chinese Female Doctor from the University of Brussels Uses the Opium Prohibition Problem as a Thesis

Miss Wang Jingqi

Brussels, July 10th communication, the former Chinese Minister to Belgium, the International Opium Prohibition Representative Miss Wang Jingqi, studied at the University of Brussels, and her graduation thesis was on the Chinese opium prohibition problem. At the beginning of the month, she gave a thesis in the University Auditorium, the final test, and public talk debate. There were five examiners, one of whom was Lea Gerard, a member of the Far East Opium Investigation Group two years ago. The debate lasted a long time. One person in the crowd stood up and questioned, saying, "In 1914, I personally saw poppies everywhere in China, which violated the Sino-British Treaty of 1907." Ms. Wang talked eloquently, saying, "At that time, most of them had already been cleared. Otherwise, the British government would have protested according to the treaty. What you saw, sir, may be a small corner of China. I hope you will not use it as an example of the whole." He then yielded. As a result, the examiners unanimously awarded her the highest degree of doctorate. The examiners have already congratulated her and represented the University of Brussels to congratulate her. Ms. Wang has been overseas for a long time, continuing her father's work to promote the country. If she returns to China and sees opium everywhere and the black disaster is rampant, she may not dare to have the courage to speak loudly and be a Chinese debater. It is said that Wang is now going to study in England, and after returning, she will continue to work to reject drugs.

Labor-Management Negotiations Resolved the Chinese Industrial Plant Labor Dispute Yesterday

The Factory Will Maintain Meals for Three Months While Temporarily Shut Down

The Contract Will Be Signed at the Social Affairs Bureau Today

The Chinese Industrial Plant on Bailinan Road, Shanghai West, has narrowed its business scope and stopped the dispute over the collection and distribution of silk fabrics in two departments. Yesterday, the labor and management sides directly negotiated and decided on a method, which was passed by the general meeting of workers. The details of each item are recorded below.

Negotiation Results At 9:00 a.m. yesterday, the Chinese Branch Office of the Silk Weaving Industry Union in the Third District dispatched representatives from various departments, including Wang Songsheng, Chen Binghui, Zhu Boying, Huang Haiqing, and others, to No. 6 Sichuan Road to directly negotiate with Chairman Liu Hongsheng and Director Xie Peide. After a long period of research, it was decided that (1) the two departments of collection and distribution of silk fabrics would temporarily stop working for three months, (2) during the shutdown period, the factory would maintain workers' meals at 6 yuan per month per person, and (3) after the three-month period expires, if the factory is unable to continue opening, the standard of dismissal compensation will be negotiated again. At that time, the labor representatives stated that the proposed method would have to wait for the afternoon meeting to solicit the opinions of all workers before a decision could be made.

Meeting Decision The labor representatives rushed back to the factory and convened a temporary general meeting of workers at 2:30 p.m. to solicit opinions. Chairman Wang Songsheng reported that the mayor had instructed them to directly negotiate with the capital director and formulate a plan. At that time, the public opinion hoped to start work immediately to maintain their livelihoods. After the chairman's repeated persuasion, the proposed method was passed.

Signing Today After the Chinese Branch Office of the Silk Weaving Industry Union in the Third District adjourned the meeting, it notified the Social Affairs Bureau by telephone at 4:00 p.m. that the labor and management sides would dispatch responsible representatives to the Social Affairs Bureau at 9:00 a.m. today to sign a settlement contract.

The Wu Song Yong'an Labor Dispute: The Labor Union Sent Representatives to Petition Yesterday

The Cotton Spinning Industry Union of the Eighth District, because the workers of Wu Song Yong'an Spinning Factory, Shen Yongming and other eight people, were acquitted by the court, the prosecutor who handled the case at that time, because he did not accept the verdict, had to appeal, so he was not allowed to post bail, which led to the death of worker Shen Fugeng in prison. Also, because the factory violated government orders and refused to allow the original workers to work in the factory, yesterday, representatives Wang Tingxi, Wang Yuncheng, Zhao Rongsheng, and others sent more than a dozen people to the local court, the Social Affairs Bureau, and the Municipal Party Department to petition, first to the Municipal Party Department, where they were received by Wang Manyun, Director of the People's Training Section. The representatives stated their intentions. Later, Wang replied that the headquarters would do its best to rescue the detained workers. As for the unemployed workers who were rejected by the factory, the headquarters would send personnel to negotiate with the factory together with the Social Affairs Bureau. The representatives then left and went to the local court to request the release of the detained workers, and Wang Daozhou, the chief clerk, replied that the court attached great importance to this case. After the last petition to the court, the judge was immediately notified to expedite the conclusion. Now that it has been acquitted, it has been sent to the prosecutor for disposal, and the court has no right to advise. Then he went to the Procuratorate and asked to release the detained workers. Prosecutor Chen replied that he had forwarded the intention to the original prosecutor for expedited disposal. The representatives then left and went to the Social Affairs Bureau to meet Wang Xianqing, Director of the Mediation Section, and stated that all the workers had been oppressed by the capital after the war and refused to work. Thousands of workers had no food and shelter, and the bureau had already ordered the capital to protect the jobs of the original workers. However, the capital dared to violate government orders and implement its means of oppressing labor. Then Director Wang replied that the bureau would decide on an effective method in the shortest time to solve this dispute as soon as possible.

Scheduled to Open on the 29th of This Month

The Shanghai County Government, in view of the recent hot weather and the prevalence of the plague, and the daily reports of the death of people infected with the plague in the county, consulted and planned to set up a temporary plague hospital so that people infected with the plague could be admitted to the hospital for rescue at any time. Japanese Ship Refuses Inspection

Third-Class Passengers Ultimately Inspected

According to the Japanese Shanghai Daily, at 4:00 p.m. on the 26th, the Nagasaki Maru entered the port and berthed at the Huishan Wharf. The Shanghai Port Authority implemented a serious and formal inspection of all passengers and crew members. However, the shipping company said that it had not received a pre-notice of the inspection, and that there was no such precedent for crew members and passengers from Japan to Shanghai. It refused the inspection and still wanted to act according to the previous practice. The ship was allowed to move freely as soon as it berthed. However, the chief quarantine officer did not allow the request. As a result, the inspectors completely inspected the third-class passengers and crew members.

Appeals from the Fresh Frozen Fish Industry

There is a Rumor of the Revival of Fish Tax

The Fresh Frozen Fish Industry Association's letter to the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce says: "Dear Sir, recently, fish merchants from Ningbo and Taizhou have been inquiring with our association, saying that there are recent rumors that there is a news of the re-imposition of fish tax, which seems to be well-founded. If it is realized, the fishermen's chance of survival will be cut off. Please help us to appeal." The fish shops under the association are also closely related and pay close attention to this matter. The rumor is spreading like wildfire. On March 28 last year, the National Government ordered that China's fishing industry is declining. If it is not actively promoted and properly protected, it will not be enough to save it and revitalize it. Therefore, all fish taxes and fishing taxes are exempted, and no agency shall establish other items to collect this tax in order to comply with the government's intention to eliminate disturbances and maintain the fishing industry. After receiving the order, the fishermen of Jiangsu and Zhejiang were grateful and said that there was hope for their livelihood. Unexpectedly, after only one year, there was a rumor of the revival of the fish tax. Woe is me, the common people, running around to tell each other, I really don't know where to start. The National Government issued a clear order to save and revitalize the fishing industry, and all fish taxes and fishing taxes were exempted, and it was repeatedly clarified that no agency shall establish other items to collect this tax. According to our normal reason, we think that we can maintain this guarantee permanently. Now the decline of the fishing industry is as old as ever. Is it said that it has been saved? Is it revitalized? No one can answer this. The government will show great faith to the people, or it will not be as changeable as the rumors say. Only the fishermen are on the verge of bankruptcy. The fishermen are exhausted inside and out, and they are no longer able to bear the pressure. Hearing this rumor, they are extremely frightened. In addition to sending a telegram to Chairman Lin of the National Government, President Wang of the Executive Yuan, and Minister Chen of the Ministry of Industry, please preside over the situation. We also send a special letter to your association, asking you to consider the pain of the fish merchants and fishermen, and quickly forward it to save them. We are deeply grateful."

Refined Salt Industry Resolved to Increase Prices

And Will Organize a Trade Association

Due to excessive costs and years of losses in the refined salt industry in this port, and the government has increased the salt tax, the industry has been greatly alarmed. Yesterday, it convened the industry and held a meeting at Jiuda Company to discuss relief measures. The attendees included Chen Canglai, representative of Jiuda, Zhang Dezai, representative of Liyuan, He Ziru, representative of Hongyuan, Wang Junfu, representative of Fuhai, Cai Junfu, representative of Yuhua, and Zhang Zhesi, representative of Tongyi. First, Chen Canglai and Zhang Dezai proposed measures. After discussion, it was decided that from August 1st, the price of Ma bags of refined salt would be 13 yuan per bag, and the price of paper-wrapped refined salt would be 14 bags per yuan. All commissions will be temporarily cancelled to maintain the cost. The industry is deeply concerned because it has suffered heavy losses in recent years, so it plans to further organize a trade association.

Local News Two

Scope of Amnesty and Commutation

There are Regulations That Cannot Be Accommodated

Family Members of Criminals Are Fortunate Not to Be Deceived

Shen Jiayi, the president of the Second Branch of the Jiangsu High Court, said that he is currently handling the amnesty, and he is deeply afraid that some people outside will take advantage of this incident to defraud the family members of general criminals. Therefore, he issued an announcement yesterday to inform the public. The announcement is copied as follows:

Announcement Regarding the announcement, the National Government promulgated the Amnesty Ordinance on June 24. The provisions on the scope of commutation are very clear. This court and the Special District Court are complying with the order. However, I am afraid that the people do not know all the details, or are fooled by others, resulting in fraud. The provisions of Article 2 of the Amnesty Ordinance are hereby announced so that the public can be informed. That is, those who committed crimes before March 5 of this year, who do not fall within the various crimes listed in that article, will naturally be commuted. If they are crimes listed in that article, they will not be commuted. The period of commutation is also stipulated by the ordinance and cannot be accommodated in the slightest. If anyone says that they can dredge up the court for commutation, it is purely fraud and extortion. They should immediately report to the Special District Court or report them. Do not misunderstand yourself. This announcement, Article 2 of the Amnesty Ordinance, in addition to those who are pardoned in accordance with the preceding article, those who commit other crimes, the most serious principal punishment for which is death, life imprisonment, or imprisonment for a term of seven years or more, the sentence is commuted by one-third, and those who are less than seven years, the sentence is commuted by one-half. However, the following crimes are not commuted: (1) those who commit treason, (2) those who kill direct ascendants, (3) those who kill out of premeditation or have cruel acts, (4) those who rob, rob, or pirate and intentionally kill, (5) those who rob, pirate, or set fire and rape, (6) those who kidnap for ransom and intentionally kill the victim or rape them, (7) those who rape and intentionally kill the victim, (8) those who transfer the abducted or lured out of the territory of the Republic of China, (9) those who commit dereliction of duty or embezzlement of public funds, (10) those who commit crimes stipulated in special criminal laws and regulations that are of the same nature as the above articles.
