First Special Court Continues Hearing of Wenying's Tragic Death Case

Wenying's Mother Arrives at Court Injured

Fan Hongsheng's Testimony Evasive

Lawyer Claims Da Tan is Mentally Ill

Diaoyu Ke Granted Bail

After the female physiognomist Wang Wenying was murdered, Hua Detective You A'gen, Su Changsheng, and Detective Zhao Ziren from the Zhabei Police Station arrested the principal culprit, Fan Hongsheng (also known as Fan Ruibao). Wang's teacher, Diaoyu Ke (i.e., Cheng Meixian), was also suspected and arrested by Detective You, and the details of their arraignment by the First Special Court have been reported in this newspaper. Yesterday morning, Judge Feng Shide of the Criminal Division opened a court session to continue the interrogation. Fan was defended by Lawyer Jiang Baoli. Lawyer Ru Baoyi of the police station presented the case, stating that after investigation, Cheng Meixian had no special relationship and should not be prosecuted, requesting his release. Wang Wenying's mother, Wang Wu, although discharged from the hospital, was not fully recovered and arrived at court injured to request questioning. Wang Wu gave her statement, speaking in the Hangzhou dialect, making it difficult to understand what she said. A slightly clearer account of her statement is recorded below: she stated that she was 54 years old, from Hangzhou, and Wenying was her biological daughter. At the age of 13, Cheng Meixian took her to Shanghai to study under the female physiognomist Ling Qing, but the art of physiognomy was entirely taught by Cheng. The following year, Cheng deflowered her daughter, and they have been living together as lovers for four years. A month ago, Cheng brought Fan Hongsheng to her house, introducing him to her daughter. On the 15th of this month (lunar calendar), Fan Hongsheng came to Wenying and said that Cheng Meixian had introduced him to her as a husband. Wenying replied that marriage was a major event and she had to agree, and Cheng Meixian could not interfere. On the 16th at noon, Fan again brought two copies of the Shen Bao newspaper, wrapped around a sharp blade. He brought the blade to Wenying to look at, saying he had to take it home. Wenying told him that if the police found it, he would be sent to court and investigated, so he should be careful. Fan then went outside, and she found his behavior suspicious. She followed him and saw Fan enter the New World Hotel (where Cheng's photography studio was located). Returning home, she blamed her daughter for associating with such people and asked her not to eat opium, as it was dangerous. That afternoon, Fan came again, saying he had been to Cheng Meixian's place, and Cheng agreed to give Wenying to him as a wife, telling Wenying, "You must break away from your mother, so she doesn't need to be consulted." Cheng also gave him 500 yuan, instructing him to kill her mother. If he could achieve the goal, then she would surely give him Wenying as his wife. Because she opposed it, Fan took out a sharp blade from his pocket, with a red string on the handle, and slashed her three times. Wenying, seeing this, shouted for the police and kept saying, "I must find you." Fan then killed Wenying. According to her estimation, if she had allowed her daughter to marry him, she would not have been injured. Fan's lawyer, Jiang Baoli, questioned her, asking if Fan appeared crazy when he came. She replied that he was quite clear-headed and handsome. The court then questioned Fan Hongsheng, who testified that he did not know Cheng Meixian, and only met him once. His affair with Wenying was not introduced by Cheng. He had a wife, but they divorced due to disagreements. He then had an affair with a woman who frequented a certain opium den in Qinghefang. A month ago, he went to the opium den to look for his mistress but did not find her. Wenying was eating red pills and was very sociable. Seeing him, she asked his name and occupation and invited him to eat four corners of red pills. She said that because her mother forced her to be a prostitute, she did not want to go home and was staying in room 225 of the New World Hotel, but did not say she was a female physiognomist. Two days later, Wenying opened rooms 11 and 12 at the Yadong Hotel and went there with him. They had a good conversation and became intimate that evening, staying together for seven days. During these seven days, Wenying never went home. Afterwards, every one or two days, they would open a hotel room, always using Yadong as their meeting place. His feelings for Wenying were very strong, and there was no hatred between them. On the day she moved to Pingle Lane, she gave him ten yuan, asking him to buy teapots and other things. Recently, a certain Mr. Jia, acquainted with the prostitute Lao Si, wanted to open a gambling table. Because Wenying was familiar with Lao Si, he went to her on the day of the incident, asking her to intercede with Lao Si for a position at the gambling table. He went a total of six times. The second time he went, she gave him five yuan, ordering him to eat at a Western restaurant. The fourth time he went, he saw a man named Cheng Wenqin in Western attire. Wenying was not killed by him. When she was killed, he was taking a bath at the Longquan Bathhouse. The court did not believe him and could investigate. Detective Su testified that he had gone to Longquan to investigate, and the tea attendant said that Fan had come at 2 PM on the afternoon of the incident and left after a while, while the incident occurred at 3:30 PM in the afternoon. The Wang family's maid, Chen A'jin, and the driver, Pan Changfu, also testified (details omitted, as reported in this newspaper). At this point, Lawyer Jiang claimed that the defendant, Fan Hongsheng, suffered from mental illness. Last year, his family sent him to the Xin Puyu Hall in the South City for treatment. He bit through the iron chain and escaped to Nanjing. His brother caught him and sent him back to the hall, but he soon escaped again and went to Suzhou, where a colleague, a station employee, sent him to the Gospel Hospital a month ago. He had another episode. According to criminal law, those who have lost their minds are exempt from punishment. However, the symptoms of mental loss are sometimes no different from normal people, and their memory is quite intact. Even the murderer who killed the French president did not show any signs of mental illness in court. The judge still felt it necessary to conduct an evaluation, so he requested the court to postpone the hearing for two weeks, allowing his lawyer to collect evidence to prove that the defendant had a mental illness and submit it to the court. He also requested the court to send the defendant to a psychiatrist for evaluation to determine whether the defendant should be held responsible. Lawyer Ru of the police station stated that since the defendant had evidence to prove his mental illness, he did not object to the request for postponement of the prosecution. Judge Feng then ordered the case to be postponed for two weeks and then heard again. Cheng Meixian was released on bail pending summons, and Fan Hongsheng was returned to custody.

Public Works Bureau Actively Proceeding with Seaside Bathing Beach

City Government Orders Compliance by Health and Other Bureaus

The seaside beach in the Gaoqiao district of this city has been a freely chosen swimming spot for Shanghai citizens and foreigners who enjoy swimming. However, the Public Works Bureau of this city believes that Shanghai residents urgently need a large-scale bathing beach in the summer, so it plans to develop the original site into a seaside bathing beach to meet actual needs. It was originally planned to add detailed equipment this summer, but due to the exhaustion of municipal funds, it could not be realized. A contingency plan for this year was temporarily devised and submitted to the municipal government for approval. The bureau had previously received Instruction No. 1661 from the municipal government, approving a trial run, and ordering compliance by the Public Security, Health, Public Works, and other bureaus. Therefore, the bureau has begun to implement it, striving to realize the contingency plan. The "Emergency Plan for Opening the Gaoqiao Seaside Bathing Beach This Year" is recorded below: (1) "Demarcation of Scope": It is planned to demarcate the entire sandy beach outside the Yu Zihao Pond near the Dragon King Temple in Gaoqiao as the seaside bathing beach area, placing wooden stakes at both ends and connecting them with lead wire as a boundary. The area within the boundary will be exclusively operated and arranged by the municipal government. Other areas must not be enclosed to avoid disputes and confusion. (2) "Life-Saving Equipment": Eight wooden stakes with water level marks will be erected at a depth of one meter and thirty-five centimeters at low tide, and red flags will be raised on them to mark the boundary between deep and shallow water, so that those who are not good at deep swimming will be warned. A lifeboat will also be stationed next to the stakes, painted red, with lifebuoys and life ropes on board for emergencies. (One lifeboat will be temporarily borrowed by this bureau.) (3) "Changing Equipment": Eighty changing rooms, each with a male and female toilet, will be installed on the grass outside the pond. Each door will have a lock and key, and a person will be specially assigned to manage it, so that bathers can change clothes and store their clothes and belongings. Each small room will be nine meters by one or two meters, enough for three or four people to use. "(4) "Rest Area": Fine sand will be laid on a suitable location on the grass-covered beach. Eight or nine sunshades, twenty canvas chairs, and eight small coffee tables will be placed for bathers to sit and rest after bathing. (5) "Cold Drink Equipment": A large wine stall with twelve meters and a small kitchen with about three by six meters will be built. The pillars and frames will be made of foreign pine, and the tops and four walls will be made of canvas so that they can be disassembled when not in use. Tables, chairs, and utensils will also be provided for the sale of beverages.

Adding Twenty-Seven Vehicles

At the end of last year, the Public Bus Company of the Public Concession submitted to the Public Works Department that it would add 50 vehicles at the beginning of this year to reduce congestion. Police Officer from the Shenjiahang Precinct Assaults a Platoon Leader of the Defense Corps

Arousing Public Outrage Among Merchants and Residents

Leading to a Strike

At the Shenjiahang Township near the city center, a police officer assaulted Wang Shisan, a platoon leader of the Defense Corps, at 4:00 PM on the previous day (the 26th), causing serious injuries. This aroused public outrage among merchants and residents, leading to a strike. It is said that the incident was caused by a villager playing the erhu (Chinese violin) to cool off in front of the Chipeide Pharmacy in Dongshi at 9:00 PM on the 24th. A police officer from Post No. 4769 of the Second Precinct of the Seventh District came forward to interfere. The villager argued that playing the erhu was not against the prohibited activities, leading to a conflict. Lu Shengxian, a shop assistant from the pharmacy, stepped forward to mediate, saying that playing the erhu was a form of entertainment. Unexpectedly, the police officer became angry with Lu, tore his shirt, and blew his whistle wildly. Merchants, residents, and members of the Defense Corps arrived to disperse the crowd. Afterwards, Lu reported the incident to the Second Precinct. The precinct chief, Yao Benyuan, was out on business, so the inspector briefly inquired about the situation and ordered Lu to leave without reprimanding the police officer. After Yao learned of this, he invited Wang Shisan, the platoon leader of the Defense Corps' branch defense station stationed in Shenjiahang, to the station for a face-to-face inquiry. Wang explained the situation in detail. Chief Yao then disciplined Officer No. 4769 by striking his palm twenty times as a warning. The officer, after being disciplined, not only did not know to repent but harbored resentment against Wang, intending to retaliate. He gathered four or five colleagues and waited with wooden sticks at the stone bridge in front of the station. When Wang said goodbye and left, walking to the bridge, the officers stepped forward, grabbed him, and beat him, causing Wang to be seriously injured. He shouted for help, and the townspeople rushed to the scene. The officers then scattered, but Wang had already fallen to the ground with serious injuries. He was helped up, sent to the Defense Corps headquarters, and then transferred to the Nanyang Hospital in this city for treatment. The merchants and residents of the town, seeing the officers acting so recklessly and unreasonably, assaulting an important official of the Defense Corps, were immediately outraged and went on strike. On one hand, the Defense Corps reported to the Defense Corps Management Committee, requesting investigation. On the other hand, they submitted a report to the municipal government and Director Wen of the Public Security Bureau, requesting strict investigation of the troublemaking officer to maintain local security.

Egg Industry Association Telegraphs Request for Investigation of Anhui Egg Tax Bureau

The Shanghai Egg Industry Association has reported that the Anhui Egg Tax Bureau was abolished by the Ministry's order, but the tax bureau still exists and continues to collect taxes, which is in violation of the central government's orders and oppression of merchants. Yesterday, they sent a telegram to the National Government's Executive Yuan and Ministry of Finance, stating, "To the esteemed Executive Yuan and Ministry of Finance in Nanjing: We have just received a telegram from the Anhui Huaining County Egg Industry Association, stating that the egg tax bureau has been abolished by the Ministry's order, and the special business tax has also been resolved to be suspended by the provincial government, but the bureau continues to collect taxes, which is unreasonable. We request the Finance Department to instruct us to investigate the egg tax in this province in accordance with Article 18 of the Ministry of Finance's revised regulations for the collection of business tax in this province. The short-term business tax should be collected. Before the special tax was handled, merchants were recruited to manage the bureau and collect taxes in June of last year. The tax rate was set at four cents per basket, which was originally stated in the regulations that egg merchants would be taxed at a rate of 20/1000 of their capital. The bureau has been collecting taxes at this rate. Now that the special tax has been suspended, the egg tax bureau continues to operate as usual and has reported to the Ministry and telegraphed instructions to that effect. Now, according to the previous situation, we must follow the instructions to urge all egg merchants to pay the taxes owed as soon as possible and not delay any further. We have repeatedly reported that the special business tax in Anhui Province was abolished by the Yuanbu order, and the egg tax bureau has also been repeatedly ordered to be abolished. On July 12 of this year, the provincial government again resolved to suspend the special business tax. The egg tax bureau has no possibility of existing. Now, the Finance Department is still setting up a bureau to collect taxes, continuing its policy of harming merchants and harming the people. We are deeply alarmed and ask for a unified resistance to solve the problem. On this basis, the egg industry is also a general business, and the business tax does not seem to need to be collected independently. In the past, it was handled by the Anhui Business Tax Collection Office in various districts. After the special business tax was implemented, it was listed as one of the eight types. Now that the special business tax has been abolished, the egg tax bureau has no reason to exist independently. Moreover, the business tax law stipulates that there is a clear distinction between business turnover and capital amount. The Finance Department deliberately calls a deer a horse, forcibly naming the value of goods as capital and levying special heavy taxes. At present, the value of each basket of Anhui eggs is 10 yuan, then the tax of 4 cents per basket reaches 40/1000, which exceeds the 2/1000 stipulated by the Anhui Provincial Business Tax Regulations by 20 times. Such harsh taxes have never been seen before. It is also said that the egg tax in this province was recruited to manage the bureau and collect taxes in June of last year. I do not know according to which laws and regulations. It is clear that the Anhui Finance Department has resumed the Lijin. This kind of contempt for the orders to abolish the Lijin has no knowledge of the Central Government. We should ask the Yuanbu to investigate strictly to respect the officialdom and re-emphasize the merit order. To be in urgent anticipation of the order, the Shanghai Egg Industry Association."

Tragedy of a Bomb Found in a Field in Dachang

Father and Son Instantly Killed

Wife and Second Son Both Seriously Injured

A local villager named Yang, who was a farmer residing in the Yangjia Village in Gujiazhai, Dachang Township, Baoshan County, was weeding in the field with his wife and two sons at around 3:00 PM yesterday afternoon. Unexpectedly, they discovered a bomb. The son picked it up and played with it, striking it with a large stone. With a loud bang, smoke filled the air. Yang and his eldest son were instantly killed on the spot, their flesh and blood indistinguishable, which was unforgettable. His wife, Yang (35 years old), was injured in her right thigh, and his second son, Xigen (9 years old), was injured in his arm. Both were seriously injured. They were sent to Renji Hospital by rickshaw for treatment.

A Rickshaw Puller's Honesty in Returning Found Money

A Rare and Admirable Deed in These Decadent Times

People from Jiangbei Should Not All Be Judged the Same

Yesterday afternoon around 5 o'clock, a rickshaw puller reported to the Third Precinct of the First District of the Municipal Public Security Bureau, claiming to be Yuan Jilang, a 19-year-old from Jiangbei, residing in Yaoyuju Alley inside Xiaonanmen in the Nanshi area. He stated that while pulling his rickshaw the previous evening around 8 o'clock near Xiaotaoyuan on Xicang Bridge, a man appearing to be in his thirties hired his rickshaw. Upon reaching Guangfu Temple, the man wanted to go to Beijing Road and Henan Road in the British Concession. Because his rickshaw did not have a Concession permit, he paid the rickshaw fare and then switched to a rickshaw with a Concession permit. Unexpectedly, in his haste when changing rickshaws, the man inadvertently left a leather wallet on his rickshaw, containing fifteen yuan in banknotes and stock certificates. After discovering this, the man and the rickshaw were nowhere to be found, making it impossible for him to return the items. However, he felt that these items did not belong to him and that he should not take unjust wealth. Therefore, he brought the original items to the bureau today, requesting instructions. After presenting the wallet, Director Jin praised Yuan for his honesty in returning the found money, deeming it commendable. He decided to temporarily keep the items at the bureau, awaiting the owner to come forward with proof of ownership.

The Local Court Changes the Title of Court Clerks to Process Servers

President Shen of the Shanghai Local Court, based on regulations to elevate the position of court clerks, specially submitted a request to the higher court to change the title of court clerks to process servers. The request has been approved by the higher court, and the title of process server has been formally adopted, hoping to expand the scope of their duties.

Robbery at the Shanghai Military Camp Yesterday Morning

Five robbers suddenly broke into the home of Huang Caiji at No. 4 Qingyan Zuonong, Dong, in the Nanshi Shanghai Military Camp yesterday. Two of the robbers were wearing short shirts and pants made of white spun silk, one was wearing a gray military uniform, resembling a soldier, and the remaining two, one wearing short shirts and pants made of blue cloth, and the other wearing a long white summer cloth gown, all spoke with local accents. After entering, they stormed into the living room. One of the robbers immediately brandished a pistol, forcing the Huang family into a corner and forbidding them from making a sound. The remaining robbers then rushed into the bedroom, ransacking chests and cabinets, stealing more than seventy yuan in banknotes and clothing and accessories, totaling over a hundred yuan. They then left the house with the stolen goods and fled.

Four Banks Issue Reserve Report

No. 234

The Four Banks Reserve Depository is jointly established by the Yanyeh, Jincheng, Zhongnan, and Dalu Banks, exclusively handling the issuance of Zhongnan Bank banknotes. In accordance with the depository's issuance regulations, the banknotes are fully backed by reserves, with cash reserves accounting for at least 60% and security reserves accounting for at most 40%. A public announcement is made weekly, verified by the auditors and accountants of the four banks. The 234th announcement of the Shanghai Reserve Depository on July 23, 1932, is recorded below: Amount of banknotes in circulation: 18,200,965.57 yuan. Amount of reserves: 18,200,965.57 yuan, including: Cash reserves: 11,237,426.87 yuan; Security reserves: 6,972,230.13 yuan.

Recent News from the Jiyi Benevolent Society's Plague Hospital

The Jiyi Benevolent Society's plague hospital, located on Tangshan Road in Hongkou, has been in operation for just over a month. However, it has already seen over 13,000 outpatients. The weather was unusually hot last week, and the hospital's outpatient services were particularly crowded. According to its weekly report, there were 3,554 outpatients, 262 cases of true cholera, and 22 cases of heatstroke. The outcomes were generally good, with 201 patients recovering and being discharged, and 5 patients succumbing without being saved. The spacious wards are already filled to capacity. The hospital is located adjacent to the war zone, and in an area where workers and commoners reside. Although this is a major factor in the busy clinical services, its comprehensive facilities, spacious buildings, experienced medical staff, and conscientious staff are not easily found in other plague hospitals. Therefore, many plague-stricken residents from the western and southern districts of the city travel long distances for treatment, further increasing the hospital's workload. It is now learned that the hospital's directors, anticipating the approach of autumn and fearing that the epidemic will spread even more severely, are actively planning to expand the facilities to strengthen the epidemic prevention efforts and will not establish separate branches in order to maintain focus.

National Physician He Nengshi Returns to Shanghai for Consultations

National Physician He Nengshi, who has a clinic at No. 479 Zha Pu Road, Hongkou, in the Banling Nan Medical Hall, fled back to Guangdong due to the outbreak of the Shanghai War. He returned to Shanghai from Guangdong last month and resumed his consultations. In anticipation of a major epidemic of cholera and diarrhea after the war, he has specially prepared an emergency remedy for immediate administration without charge. Many patients have been cured quickly. Dr. He is charitable and sets a consultation fee of one yuan, waiving it for the poor. He is known to all sectors of society and the poor and sick.

Meeting Record of the Ruifeng Lane Tenants' Association

The Ruifeng Lane Tenants' Association held its second general meeting of members yesterday, attended by over a hundred members, as well as Zhou Xinyou, representative of the Housing Associations Federation, and Chen Jiufeng, representative of Ruiqing, Ruiyu, and Ruikang, three lanes. The meeting began with Chairman Huang Junfu reporting the purpose of the meeting and the financial situation. Then Zhou Xinyou, Chen Jiufeng, and others gave speeches (details omitted). Then, the following proposals were made: (1) Representatives should be appointed to directly negotiate rent reduction with the landlords. (2) Before a compromise is reached in the negotiations, rent payments should be suspended and the rent money deposited in the bank. (3) Revise the association's charter. (4) Actively establish sanitation, fire prevention, education, and public safety measures. All were passed and handed over to the executive committee for handling.

To the Editor: The news item published in your newspaper today regarding the scheduled relocation of the Shanghai County Government and the statement that the original county site on Penglai Road has been publicly put up for unlimited price bidding is completely inconsistent with the facts. Upon investigation, the old site of this County Government has not been put up for bidding, and the construction of the new site is underway. The relocation date has not yet been determined. Please make a correction. Sincerely, The Shanghai County Government, July 27th.

Supplement to the Local Edition of Shen Bao

Commentary

Forcing Oneself to Be a Daughter-in-Law and the Issue of Chastity

— Fo

Although the issue of chastity is fundamentally untenable in the modern trend, there are no explicit legal restrictions on women maintaining chastity, because chastity is a moral issue and not a legal one.

The case of Ma Baolin, a student at Suzhou County Middle School, and his fiancée, Xu Caizhen, a female vocational student, both taking poison has occurred. Ma died from the poison, while Xu was saved by medical treatment. Subsequently, Xu, as the fiancée, requested to observe chastity for Ma, but Ma's family firmly refused. Xu Caizhen then engaged in a physical altercation with Ma's stepmother, Zhang, each sustaining minor injuries, leading to a lawsuit. Xu Caizhen's willingness to observe chastity for Ma Baolin as his fiancée in this world of "shifting allegiances" and "every man for himself" can be seen as an attempt to correct the shallow customs and encourage virtuous practices.

However, it is not fashionable. Furthermore, being a martyr is easy, but being a chaste widow is difficult. A martyr is simply driven by momentary passion, reckless of personal safety, either taking poison or cutting one's throat, which is relatively easy to do. But a chaste widow requires a state of mind where "my heart is like an ancient well, and no waves will ever rise," which is extremely difficult to achieve. Being young and with one's will not yet firmly decided, the environment can easily tempt and shake one's heart. Enduring hardship and swallowing bitterness is not human. It was easier to maintain chastity in the past than it is now. In the past, women did not leave their homes, and there were fewer temptations from adverse environments. Now, with open social interactions, those who do not become disordered when they do not see something desirable may not be so when they do see something desirable. Rather than having a good beginning and a poor ending, why bother?

In the past, unmarried women would hold memorial tablets and perform the role of a relative for their deceased fiancés. However, such inhumane actions are unbearable and were viewed as excessive even at the time. Since they were unmarried, they had not fully acquired the status of a wife, so observing chastity was unnecessary. Xu Caizhen's lack of obligation to observe chastity is even more obvious. Even if her request were reluctantly granted after Ma's family refused, how could she live a peaceful life? Furthermore, their son chose to take his own life due to her rebuke, so how could his daughter-in-law live in peace with them for long? It is unlikely. Going a step further, if she wants to observe chastity, there is no need to go through the door. She can simply remain unmarried at home and vow never to marry for the rest of her life, which would be sufficient to face her deceased fiancé in the afterlife. Why go through the door before claiming to observe chastity?

In this case of an unmarried couple taking poison together, the reason for taking poison is perhaps not just because of the stepmother's rebuke, but perhaps there are other reasons, although this is still unknown. If the unmarried couple did not experience other forms of abuse from the stepmother, and only died because of a rebuke, then their death can be said to be without reason. If the stepmother was usually harsh and difficult to live with, making them prefer to die, then why would Xu Caizhen insist on going through the door to observe chastity? These contradictory reasons are truly incomprehensible!

Literature and Art

Feelings at the Barracks, Following Songfu's Rhyme

— Yun

Remains of the fortress still show traces of battle,

Reflecting on the past adds to my sorrow.

Even a commoner has responsibility for his country's fate,

If I don't avenge the public, my hatred won't abate.

Winds and clouds shift, mixing yin and yang,

Recalling the past fills me with a hundred emotions.

Reading about ancient battlefields,

Gods wail and ghosts cry in sorrowful lamentations.

Gazing at the mountains and rivers after the calamity,

Who will bury the innocent victims of cruelty?

Where are the tall buildings and grand mansions now?

Jade and stone are burned into a pile of ashes.

Science

Method of Making Mirrors

— Lü Ziwei

The procedure for making mirrors can be divided into four sections: (A) materials, (B) liquid preparation, (C) silvering, and (D) finishing.

(A) The most suitable glass for making mirrors is glass about two or three tenths of an inch thick. Choose glass that is free of air bubbles and flat. Potassium glass is best. First, wash it with ammonia water or sodium carbonate water to remove oil stains, then wipe it clean with a wet cloth in water, and finally wash it with distilled water.

(B) Silvering liquids use potassium sodium tartrate, tartaric acid, or fructose. Tartaric acid is the most suitable. The method is to first prepare two liquids, A and B. Liquid A is made by dissolving one mace of neutral silver nitrate in ten liang of water (1% concentration). Then, gradually add ammonia water to precipitate it. Filter to remove dirt and place it in a bottle. Keep the bottle in a dark place for up to a week. Liquid B is made by dissolving two fen of silver nitrate in ten liang of boiling water. Add 1.66 fen of potassium sodium tartrate to make a tea-colored solution. While it is still hot, put it into a bottle and strain to remove residue.

(C) Remove the glass from the water and wipe it dry with a dry cloth. Mix equal amounts of liquids A and B and quickly pour them onto the surface of the glass. Use chopsticks to spread it across the entire surface. It will turn from rose color to red to dark, and in about 30 minutes, it will become a beautiful golden light.

(D) After the silver plating above dries, gently apply imitation lacquer to make it resistant to friction. Then, apply varnish, and then it is complete, becoming a useful mirror.

Society Improvement Discussion Group

My Opinion on "Improving the Marriage System"

— Wu

After reading Mr. Zhang Dingming's "Suggestions for Improving the Marriage System" in this publication, I feel the need to speak. However, for the sake of convenience of publication, I can only briefly and concretely state my views below.

First, we must study the economic relationship of the Chinese marriage system.

It is undeniable that all social phenomena cannot exist without economic relations. Because there must first be a certain form of economic foundation, and then there will be certain forms of phenomena corresponding to it. Needless to say, China's modern economy is entirely a private system. Not only that, but it is also deeply mired in semi-feudalism. That is to say, China's economy, under the pressure of imperialism, does not have the possibility of fully embarking on the path of capitalism, although some major cities have capitalist forms. Under this keynote, the feudal and private household economy is individually seized by the heads of households. Of course, the individual heads of households therefore have absolute authority in the family, and their relationship with their children is entirely one of domination and subordination. Everything of the dominated and enslaved children cannot escape the shackles of the head of the household who holds all the economy. Of course, the marriage of the children cannot be an exception. Then this illustrates the origin of marriage systems such as "parents' orders" and "matchmaker's words." For example, using children's marriages as rewards for official careers, or turning children's marriages into commodities and trading them with those who are beneficial to oneself can be found fully exemplified in modern Chinese society. Regarding this point, Mr. Zhang has explained in detail the "evils of the old marriage system," so I will not repeat them. The above is only to explain the reasons why it is so.

As mentioned above, in the modern economic system where people eat people, if we want to reform the marriage system, which is one of the deformed phenomena, I think that no matter how detailed the plan is, the result will only be "improvement"; and even just an ideal that cannot be realized in reality.

"The marriage standard of the era should not be mixed with material ... conditions." That's right, being "prudent in the beginning" may "not lead to painful results," but in this feudal and capitalist "deformed society," everything has its material conditions, especially Chinese women who have never had economic status. Can they rely on marriage to obtain material needs from their husbands? Even considering women in Shanghai, which is full of capitalism, how many are able to live independently without seeking help from their husbands? Conversely, Chinese women are always transferred to the ties of their husbands under the state of parental rewards or transactions. This is a huge "material conditions" problem. Needless to say, this issue has not been resolved in the slightest with the great revolution. Even after fully "examining" or "investigating," or "experimenting" and "understanding" the "character," "academic ability," "love power," and "family situation," can their love not change along with the inevitable changes in material conditions?

Therefore, the marriage system problem is always a branch of the economic problem, and the economic problem must be resolved with a thorough revolution. The prerequisites for China have not been resolved. The "marriage system" of its branch problems, no matter to what extent it is "improved," is at most just "improvement."

As for if the prerequisite problem has been thoroughly resolved, that is, the economic form is no longer feudal or capitalistic, then marriage is no longer bound by material conditions, and of course, there is no need for any form to restrict it. Cohabitation is possible when love matures, because organic love is by no means something that can be restricted.

Finally, I hope that this point of view can arouse widespread and heated discussion.

Park Night

— Yiping

This seductive park night was originally the paradise of old students during my student days. When I embarked on the path of life, all the youth life was subdued by the cry of bread. Parks, dance halls, and love were as vague as dreams.

Last night, I visited my good friend T after marriage. Their small family was next to Lafayette Road, the mysterious street of the concession. At the end of the conversation, they shouted to go to the park. I followed them without expressing an opinion.

Stepping into the gate of the park, I seemed to flip open my diary. The past life awakened from the mist. The stream and the secluded path were all the old places where I wandered alone. Now, they are full of the fragrant traces of ladies. Pairs and pairs, whispering like warblers, add so much enchanting light to the park. My consciousness is finally like the unrecoverable regret of losing my childhood. Walking slowly with broken moon shadows, I felt a hidden pain in my heart, like iron heels pressing on my heart.

We walked bit by bit, each with different emotions. A burst of singing came from the pavilion. Ohl MyDearl My Lovel. I shivered and watched Mr. and Mrs. T climb up the steps, embracing each other. I sat down on the chair by the side of the road. The moonlight shone on me, and the shadow slanted on the side of the road. I smiled and thanked her. The shadow never left me in my life, and at the same time, I thanked the kindness of the moonlight.

"Ping, what's wrong?" T found that I had not gone to the pavilion and returned to ask me.

"I'm tired," I lied, unwilling to spoil the beautiful scenery.

They left me, and I walked out of the park gate in a daze. Looking back at the park, it was dark and gloomy like hell. The dreams that awakened from the mist were once again called back by the demon of bread.

I took a long breath and flew onto the rickshaw and returned home like fleeing.

Sexual Issues

Remarriage

— Shizhi

In a certain unprogressive town | my hometown | recently, a widow remarried. Because of the constraints of old etiquette, she was inevitably criticized by the people of the town; especially the elders of the eighteenth century. But I tried my best to explain it for her, and believed that she was brave and had perseverance.

The fact is this: The widow, Ms. S, is a member of the intellectual class. She received higher education and is now a grade teacher in a certain primary school in Shanghai, and her monthly salary is also fifty or sixty yuan. But her family was very poor in the past, so all her expenses during her studies were provided by her deceased husband, Mr. W. The two of them were engaged from childhood, and they studied together before marriage, and their relationship was very harmonious. Later, Ms. S and Mr. W graduated from a certain university at the same time, and the two officially married. Unfortunately, on the seventh day after the marriage. Mr. W, Ms. S's only husband, died of overwork, resulting in an illness. When Mr. W was dying, he含沪 ordered his beloved Ms. S: Do not ask her to keep her vows for him, and sacrifice the happiness of her life, but hope that she will always protect his old mother | her mother-in-law | only.

After Mr. W died, Ms. S, although she thought of her husband's warmth and consideration, was so sad that she wanted to die. But for the sake of the family's economic relations, she taught in a primary school in Shanghai. She lived her lonely and depressed life very peacefully to maintain her mother-in-law's life. Although her mother-in-law died for her lovely son, she got such a virtuous daughter-in-law, and she got a lot of comfort in her heart.

Ms. S spent six years of depressed life like this, and she was confident that she was worthy of her deceased husband's love.

Recently, she thought of the darkness of the future, she felt the hunger of sex; and she was influenced by the trend; she saw Ms. Tao and Principal Jiang struggling and combining, which caused a sensation for a while. Because of the above reasons: she made her resolutely engage in a formal engagement with Mr. K, whom she considered satisfactory, in order to fix her future and solve her sexual problems.

Indeed. Keeping the vows is cruel, especially for Ms. S, who is in her youth, so I sympathize with Ms. S's remarriage this time, and I hope they will have a good marriage soon!

However, after Ms. S remarries, she will inevitably break away from her previous mother-in-law, so who will maintain her mother-in-law's life again? Therefore, I finally hope that Ms. S will continue to maintain the life of her previous mother-in-law under whatever name, so that it can be justified in terms of reason and conscience,

One opium pipe, one opium lamp, one opium tray, a small amount of opium ash, two opium picks, and thirty-nine small packets of opium are all confiscated. ▲ The case of Zhou Youchang and others versus Wang Lianfa for disruption of family; this case is dismissed. ▲ The General Police Station suing Yu A'wu for theft; Yu A'wu is fined five yuan for misappropriating property that was not in his possession. ▲ The Laozha Police Station suing Wang Xiangtao for snatching; Wang Xiangtao is sentenced to three months of imprisonment for snatching. ▲ The General Police Station suing Li A'wu for theft; Li A'wu, a repeat offender, is sentenced to eight months of imprisonment for theft. ▲ The Laozha Police Station suing Ding Wangshi for abduction; Ding Wangshi is sentenced to two months of imprisonment with a two-year reprieve for enticing a virtuous woman to sell herself for profit. ▲ The Laozha Police Station suing Wang Huanan for kidnapping for ransom; Wang Huanan is sentenced to life imprisonment for each of the two crimes of kidnapping and ransom, to be executed as life imprisonment. ▲ The General Police Station suing Tan Fucai for assault; Tan Fucai is sentenced to one year of imprisonment for using methods likely to cause death to injure a person. Three iron bars and one axe are confiscated. ▲ The Laozha Police Station suing Han Wenyu and others for using forged documents; Han Wenyu is sentenced to two months of imprisonment for using forged documents, and five forged New New Company vouchers are confiscated. Chen Xinzhang and Chen Fuquan are both found not guilty. ▲ The Xinzha Police Station suing Lu Gengsheng and others for opium offenses; Lu Gengsheng is sentenced to two months of imprisonment and fined 30 yuan for the crime of smoking opium. Zhou Guanqing and Cai Jinsheng are found not guilty, and the smoking paraphernalia is confiscated. ▲ The Jiaxing Road Police Station suing Long Zhuguo and others for theft; Long Zhuguo, a repeat offender, is sentenced to one year of imprisonment for each of the three crimes of theft, to be executed as one year and six months of imprisonment. Chen Xiaogen, a repeat offender, is sentenced to one year of imprisonment for each of the two crimes of theft, to be executed as one year and two months of imprisonment. ▲ The Hongkou Police Station suing Zhang Yunquan and others for opium offenses; Zhang Yunquan, with the intention of profiting, is sentenced to one year of imprisonment and fined 60 yuan for operating a establishment for people to smoke opium, and is a repeat offender. Fan A'er is sentenced to four months of imprisonment and fined 30 yuan for smoking opium and is a repeat offender. One opium pipe, along with red pills, are all confiscated. ▲ The Hongkou Police Station suing Li Hongshi for opium offenses; Li Hongshi, with the intention of profiting, is given a reduced sentence of six months of imprisonment with a three-year reprieve for operating a establishment for people to smoke opium. Zhou A'zhen is sentenced to three months of imprisonment and fined 50 yuan for smoking opium and is a repeat offender. The opium smoking paraphernalia is confiscated. ▲ The Huishan Police Station suing Qian Xuen and others for kidnapping for ransom; Qian Xuen, Ji Jinhua, and Wang A'lin are each sentenced to death for jointly kidnapping for ransom. Jiang Jingui is given a reduced sentence of eighteen years of imprisonment for jointly kidnapping for ransom. The number of days detained before the judgment is finalized will be counted as one day of imprisonment for every two days of detention. One handgun is stored in the warehouse pending retrieval, and two bullets are confiscated. ▲ The Yulin Police Station suing Xu Youde for theft; Xu Youde is found not guilty. ▲ The Hongkou Police Station suing Wu Jinfu for using counterfeit currency; Wu Jinfu is fined 60 yuan for using general currency banknotes that he later knew to be counterfeit. One counterfeit Bank of China banknote is confiscated. ▲ The Laozha Police Station suing Liang Zhuocai and others for gambling; Yin Qingfu, Liang Zhuocai, A'mao, Chen Guangtai, Li De, Zhao Genlin, Shen Ruilin, Chen Deming, Zhang Bingsheng, Liang Po, Wang Song, Chen Qiang, Ye Linsheng, Chen Ronggen, and Qi Baozhen are each fined 60 yuan for gambling. If converted to imprisonment, it will be calculated at three yuan per day. Gambling funds and gambling paraphernalia will be confiscated according to the list. ▲ The Public Concession Mixed Court re-examining the case of Lu Laosan and others for robbery; Lu Laosan is sentenced to five years of imprisonment for each of the four crimes of robbery, to be executed as seven years of imprisonment. The number of days spent in prison before the judgment is finalized will be counted towards the execution of the sentence. Gu Huilai is sentenced to five years of imprisonment for each of the two crimes of robbery, to be executed as six years of imprisonment. The number of days spent in prison before the judgment is finalized will be counted towards the execution of the sentence. ▲ The Public Concession Mixed Court suing Tian Jingyang and others for robbery; Tian Jingyang and Xu Quanfu are each sentenced to five years of imprisonment for each of the four crimes of robbery, to be executed as seven years of imprisonment. The number of days spent in prison before the judgment is finalized will be counted towards the execution of the sentence. Zhao Heju is sentenced to five years of imprisonment for each of the five crimes of robbery, to be executed as eight years of imprisonment. The number of days spent in prison before the judgment is finalized will be counted towards the execution of the sentence. ▲ The Hongkou Police Station suing Chen Qiang and others for opium offenses; Chen Qiang, with the intention of profiting, is sentenced to six months of imprisonment and fined 60 yuan for operating a establishment for people to smoke opium. Xiao Yuan is sentenced to one month of imprisonment and fined 20 yuan for smoking opium. Tang Rulin and Run are each sentenced to two months of imprisonment and fined 40 yuan for repeat opium smoking. The smoking paraphernalia, etc., will be confiscated according to the list. ▲ The Hongkou Police Station suing Wang A'chun for theft; Wang A'chun, a repeat offender, is sentenced to four months of imprisonment for each of the three crimes of theft, to be executed as six months of imprisonment. ▲ The Hongkou Police Station suing Zhang A'bao for theft; Zhang A'bao is sentenced to six months of imprisonment for the crime of theft. ▲ The Yangshupu Police Station suing Xia Zhongquan and others for intimidation; Xia Zhongquan, Xin Jinsheng, and Zhu Gengsheng are each sentenced to two months of imprisonment for joint intimidation. ▲ The Huishan Police Station suing Song Guangyou and others for opium offenses; Song Guangyou, Wang Ziming, Xu Longbin, and Jiang Lishi are each sentenced to one month of imprisonment and fined 10 yuan for smoking opium. The opium smoking paraphernalia is confiscated. ▲ The Huishan Police Station suing Yu Geshi for opium offenses; Yu Geshi is fined 50 yuan for possessing opium and smoking paraphernalia with the intent to use them for criminal purposes. The opium and smoking paraphernalia are confiscated. ▲ The Hongkou Police Station suing Zhu Guidao for theft; Zhu Guidao, a repeat offender, is sentenced to one month of detention for theft. ▲ The Laozha Police Station suing Zhang Gentao for assault; Zhang Gentao is sentenced to one month of detention for assaulting a person. ▲ The Huisi Police Station suing Qian A'qing for theft; Qian A'qing is sentenced to twenty days of detention for the crime of theft. ▲ The Huisi Police Station suing Hu Xiaobao for theft; Hu Xiaobao, a repeat theft offender, is sentenced to two months of imprisonment. ▲ The Xinzha Police Station suing Miao Yisheng for assault; Miao Yisheng is given a reduced sentence of one month of imprisonment for assaulting a person. ▲ The Yulin Road Police Station suing Zhao Taotao for theft; Zhao Taotao is sentenced to two months of imprisonment for repeated theft. ▲ The Yangshupu Police Station suing Qiu Fuyou; Qiu Fuyou, Wang A'gen, and Wang Quanging are each fined 20 yuan for the crime of joint gambling. The gambling paraphernalia and gambling funds are confiscated. ▲ The Yulin Road Police Station suing Shi Xiuqi for theft, etc.; Shi Xiuqi is sentenced to two months of imprisonment for the crime of theft, and two months of imprisonment for using violence and coercion against a public official while performing his duties, to be executed as three months of imprisonment. ▲ The Laozha Police Station suing Jin Rongsheng for forging documents; Jin Rongsheng is sentenced to two months of imprisonment for forging documents. ▲ The Hongkou Police Station suing Sun Rongfang for theft; Sun Rongfang is found not guilty. ▲ The Laozha Police Station suing Gu Xishan for fraud; Gu Xishan, a repeat offender, is sentenced to three months of imprisonment for each of the two crimes of fraudulently obtaining property, to be executed as four months of imprisonment. ▲ The Xinzha Police Station suing Guo Yunqiao and others for receiving stolen goods; Guo Yunqiao is fined 100 yuan for buying stolen goods, and Zhu Shenglin is fined 200 yuan for receiving stolen goods. ▲ The Gordon Road Police Station suing Ge Yunqing for opium offenses; Ge Yunqing is fined 150 yuan for possessing opium. The opium will be confiscated according to the list. ▲ The Laozha Police Station suing Su Qian for possession of opium; Su Qian is fined 100 yuan for possessing opium. The opium will be confiscated according to the list. ▲ The Gordon Road Police Station suing Ji Hongsheng, a repeat offender, is sentenced to four months of imprisonment for theft. ▲ The Gordon Road Police Station suing Liu Yutai for stolen goods; Liu Yutai, a guarantor of stolen goods, is sentenced to two months of imprisonment. ▲ The Huisi Police Station suing Zhang Youqing for theft; Zhang Youqing, a repeat offender, is sentenced to four months of imprisonment for theft. ▲ The Laozha Police Station suing Bu Wancai for theft; Bu Wancai is sentenced to two months of imprisonment for theft. ▲ The Laozha Police Station suing Chen Yingquan for theft; Chen Yingquan, a repeat offender, is sentenced to three months of imprisonment for theft. ▲ The Huisi Police Station suing Yin Daqing for assault; Yin Daqing is sentenced to two months of imprisonment for assaulting a person. ▲ The Huisi Police Station suing Zhang Jinhai for theft; Zhang Jinhai is given a reduced sentence of one month of imprisonment for theft. The number of days detained will be counted as one day of imprisonment for every two days of detention. ▲ The Xinzha Police Station suing Wang Guansheng for assault; Wang Guansheng is fined 50 yuan for assaulting a person. ▲ The Laozha Police Station suing Li A'er for assault; Li A'er and Ren Jiufu are each fined 30 yuan for jointly assaulting a person. ▲ The Hongkou Police Station suing Wu Yuanhua for theft; Wu Yuanhua is sentenced to four months of imprisonment for repeated theft. Zhang Chongtai is found not guilty. ▲ The Jing'an Temple Police Station suing Yuan Wenlong for theft; Yuan Wenlong is sentenced to two months of imprisonment for theft. ▲ The Yangshupu Police Station suing Xu Haiqing and others for assault; Xu Haiqing and Zhou Xiangxiu are each fined 60 yuan for jointly assaulting a person. Xu Haiqing is sentenced to ten days of detention for using indecent language in a public place. ▲ The Hongkou Police Station suing Du Wenhai and others for embezzlement; Du Wenhai and Du Xiangyun are each sentenced to two months of imprisonment for joint embezzlement.

Shanghai Local Court

▲ Criminal Court Judgments: The original judgment regarding Zhao Shichang, Guan Ce, Liu Guan Jiang's crimes in the case of Zhao Shichang and others appealing against the charges of obstructing official duties and opium is overturned. Zhao Shichang, Guan Ce, and Liu Guan Jiang are all found not guilty. Jiang Xushi's appeal is dismissed. Jiang Xushi's sentence of a two-year reprieve is upheld. ▲ The judgment in the case of Lu Yongfa and others for opium offenses: Lu Yongfa is sentenced to six months of imprisonment and fined 20 yuan for operating a establishment for people to smoke opium with the intention of profiting, and is also sentenced to two months of imprisonment and fined 10 yuan for smoking opium. The combined sentence is set at seven months of imprisonment and a fine of 25 yuan. Zhang Youlin is sentenced to two months of imprisonment and fined 10 yuan for smoking opium. The number of days detained before the judgment is finalized will be counted as one day of imprisonment for every two days of detention. ▲ The judgment in the case of Geng Chenshi and others for embezzlement: Geng Chenshi is sentenced to three months of imprisonment for embezzling property held in the course of business. The number of days detained before the judgment is finalized will be counted as one day of imprisonment for every two days of detention. Ren A'si is found not guilty. ▲ The judgment in the case of Shen Jinsheng for disrupting marriage: Shen Jinsheng is sentenced to two months of imprisonment for having illicit relations with a married woman. The number of days detained before the judgment is finalized will be counted as one day of imprisonment for every two days of detention. ▲ The judgment in the case of Shen Jiarong for fraud: Shen Jiarong is fined 20 yuan for using fraudulent means to induce a person to hand over property belonging to them. The number of days detained before the judgment is finalized will be counted as one yuan per day of detention. The judgment in the case of Gong Longqi for obstructing official duties: Gong Longqi is sentenced to one month of imprisonment for using violence and coercion against a public official while performing his duties in accordance with the law. The number of days detained before the judgment is finalized will be counted as one day of imprisonment for every two days of detention. ▲ The judgment in the case of Zong Xingtang appealing against the charge of misappropriating a seal: the original judgment is overturned, and Zong Xingtang is acquitted. ▲ The judgment in the case of Zhang A'er for theft: Zhang A'er is sentenced to four months of imprisonment for theft. The number of days detained before the judgment is finalized will be counted as one day of imprisonment for every two days of detention. ▲ The judgment in the case of Huang Kuilang and others for opium offenses: Huang Kuilang is sentenced to six months of imprisonment for operating a establishment for people to smoke opium with the intention of profiting, and is also sentenced to three months of imprisonment for smoking opium. The combined sentence is set at eight months of imprisonment. The number of days detained before the judgment is finalized will be counted as one day of imprisonment for every two days of detention. ▲ In the Huang Kuilang opium case, Yan Sannan and Zhao Mingkui are each sentenced to two months of imprisonment for smoking opium. The number of days detained before the judgment is finalized will be counted as one day of imprisonment for every two days of detention. ▲ The judgment in the case of Yang Youlin and others for opium offenses: Yang Youlin and Xie Jianxin are each sentenced to one year of imprisonment and fined 200 yuan for transporting opium with the intention of selling it. ▲ The number of days detained before the judgment is finalized will be counted as one day of imprisonment for every two days of detention. Yin Ji is sentenced to two years of imprisonment and fined 400 yuan for transporting opium with the intention of selling it. The number of days detained before the judgment is finalized will be counted as one day of imprisonment for every two days of detention. Zhao Jihe is sentenced to one year of imprisonment for assisting in the transport of opium with the intention of selling it. The number of days detained before the judgment is finalized will be counted as one day of imprisonment for every two days of detention. 1,458 taels of opium are confiscated. ▲ The judgment in the case of Wang Wenxiang for disruption of family: Wang Wenxiang is sentenced to one year of imprisonment for enticing a male under the age of twenty to leave the person exercising parental rights. The number of days detained before the judgment is finalized will be counted as one day of imprisonment for every two days of detention. ▲ The judgment in the case of Ling Jinfu for robbery: Ling Jinfu is sentenced to three years and six months of imprisonment for robbery in a residential home at night with a group of three or more. The number of days detained before the judgment is finalized will be counted as one day of imprisonment for every two days of detention. ▲ The judgment in the case of Chen Lizhong suing Zhou Xuelian for suspected theft and fraud: This private prosecution is dismissed. ▲ The judgment in the case of Yu A'san for intimidation: Yu A'san is sentenced to thirty days of detention for attempting to induce a person to hand over property by means of sexual intimidation with the intention of unlawfully possessing it for himself. The number of days detained before the judgment is finalized will be counted as one day of detention for every two days of detention. ▲ The judgment in the case of Ni Cairong and others for disruption of family: Ni Cairong and Lu A'zong are each sentenced to three months of imprisonment for jointly enticing a woman under the age of twenty to leave the person exercising guardianship. The number of days detained before the judgment is finalized will be counted as one day of imprisonment for every two days of detention. ▲ The judgment in the case of Cao Zhoushi and others for obstruction and false accusation: Cao Zhoushi, Tang Zhangshi, and Tang Chenshi are all found not guilty. ▲ The judgment in the case of Wang Guangzhang for disruption of family: Wang Guangzhang is sentenced to six months of imprisonment for enticing a woman under the age of twenty to leave the person exercising parental rights with the intention of having illicit relations. The number of days detained before the judgment is finalized will be counted as one day of imprisonment for every two days of detention. (July 27th)
